Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly is as we show it in front, and that for the back is olive-shaped, according to what was placed before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling around the joints
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the joints swell in a person with gout and are full of yellow crystals, it is necessary to apply the cautery on the back of the foot between the index finger and the ring finger; and move your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too far on the circumference, otherwise it would remove the yellow crystals, and apply the cautery according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After doing this on both legs, apply two cauterizations on each leg at the tip of the cuticle; and make the cauterizations along their length, one in front of the knee and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and let the cauterizations remain for a long time without curing them until the bile comes out; after this, perform the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	From memory
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the belly's solution comes from cold and moisture, as long as the retaining and digesting virtues that are in the stomach and intestines are overwhelmed, they cannot be cured by usual treatments; you see the patient suffering greatly and with much virtue, so do this. One large cautery on the stomach according to what was discussed earlier or the gastric cautery, at the circulating cautery; and three small cauterizations around the subtle mouth, for each one of .i cauteries clavile subtle, and four cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moister being abundant and the patient suffering, do this: one cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each elbow, and two small cauterizations on the stomach close to the large one. For the cure is beneficial when there's good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	Regarding the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the abscesses are beneath or around, and are old, and contain large cold and moist putrefied fluids, and if they do not respond to treatment as we have said in divisions, then apply cautery: III on the spinal bone of the back, exactly at the point that is completely beyond the place where the kidneys sit bit by bit in a triangular pattern, and use one cautery just below the navel II inches; and if you think that the stomach has cooled down, and the meat does not cook, and it can be seen swelling the abdomen, then apply I large cautery on the stomach as was previously mentioned, and another on the liver, and another under the ribs with all the cautery; and leave the cautery in place for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment until it becomes healthy.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Regarding the inflammation known as 'thelul'
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you perform surgery, if you ignite the cautery that seems to be one of the blades and then place it fully on fire over the place where you are cutting; leave your hand in such a way that the heat from the cautery reaches the base of the vein, from which the blood flows out. Do this once or twice, and if there is much fat involved, cauterize each part just as we have instructed; after using treatments that benefit afterwards wait until they are healed. And if you use a large cautery on fatty areas, it will provide more help.
de plaie mal curee	from poorly treated wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient's body cannot endure cutting or incision, as we will describe in its place, if there arises a disease that cannot be cured except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	If there is no fistula, and it decays and festers due to corrupted pus and moisture, if you need to test it with a complete method, and ensure that you know the entire technique as to how many parts it has.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After preparing the cautery as it seems suitable, and inserting it into the fistula according to its quantity, continue with the cautery until the corroded and rotten parts are burned out. Once, or twice, or three times depending on your need; and be careful not to burn nerves which are nearby, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula extends into the bladder or intestine, be cautious with these points, and do not perform it outside its natural place. Remember that it should not go through a person's body; after treating the area until it heals, and if the skin is intact, and the substances are osteous for a long time, then you know that the skin is entirely healed. And if the substances are not osteous, know that the fistula has been three times, and the bone is corrupted at the bottom; and like one of these we will mention in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Regarding kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the abdominal pain originates from the kidneys and due to large wind, it affects women more so than men, then you must perform a cautery on both sides of the kidneys with an iron rod as we have previously described; and if we apply the cautery centrally, there will be three lines of cauterization, which will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	From the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is thick and weak from heat and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then apply a cautery to the lower part of the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one on each side, and let each cautery be as long as your fist; and do one behind the back, or two if you need them; and make the cauteries in a cross shape according to the form described before.
de la marris	Of the mare's urine
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the mare's heat is cold and moist, and fails to allow conception, and her flowers are rotten with delayed termination; and when they come, she feels great pain: then it should be that you apply three cauterizations inside the womb, as we have said or like the bladder cautery, and two cauterizations behind the back; and make the cauterizations in a cross shape, as we have said.
de la hainche	From the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous mucus descends into the hip socket, and due to this reason it moves out of its place. The signs are that one leg is longer than the other when measured together; and when you find the knee at the point where you would see it normally, you should cauterize the hip socket with a fire cautery similar to half-circle shape. And mark in front of the thigh as she turns, so that the socket is inside the circle. And let the cautery be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the fire cautery is not at your disposal, make three large olive-shaped cauteries, and let these cauteries also be perfectly round like all the knuckles. And treat it while it remains sound.
de la dolor de la hainche	The pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the thigh bone area, and this is due to coldness and moisture, and the treatment is as we have discussed for division and cure failures, and the illness is old: then you must cleanse the patient of large thick body fluids with pus-filled pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After you perform the cautery; and the method of applying the cautery is according to two methods: that is to say, mixture of burning drugs, and fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	The fire cautery can be done in several ways, among which one method is: you apply three triangular cauterizations according to this form, and make sure they have good depth and size, with space the width of two between each cautery, and all are olive-shaped; no central cautery is made in the middle of the hipbone because then there would be four following this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the circle cauterization as we've mentioned before in relation to hip joint dislocations; but do it this way so that all the hips are contained within the circles, and all parts of the bone burn.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used in sciatica, when pain remains in the hip and does not reach to the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes up to the thigh and leg, then apply two cauterizations there where the patient says the pain is holding them back, and three cauterizations above the ankle four times, a little on the left side; and use cutting cauterization techniques, burn off any thickness near the knee; and should the patient feel that the pain extends up to mid-foot or almost all the way down, then apply cauterization where they sense the pain for three points or four at each point of the 'point' named cauterizations.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if more work is needed, then do it; and if the pain extends from the knee towards the thigh, use a cutaneous or circular cautery on that area, and make sure you take good care in all your cauterizations so as not to leave them incomplete such that you burn nerves and major arteries, and do not cause the patient any greater discomfort or constriction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who performed cauterization on the ankle near the foot, and it worked until their leg was completely healed, and even the toes as well, causing them to be pierced and corrupted entirely.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal treatment from which they died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a cautery on one and on the other, according to this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sage says concerning the cautery on the hip, as follows: make it in shape of such an iron rod that it's just as thick as a carpenter's axe or slightly less, and place it so that it goes through and is also about twice its thickness from one end to the other; have the parts of the instrument intersect each other halfway, and ensure these intersections are approximately half the length of your fist; make sure they curve like knots, and have iron rings precisely made; this is how it should be formed.
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it heat until it becomes entirely red and gives off smoke, and then place it on the spot of the disease in the buttock, turning it towards the healthy side. And apply a single cauterization using one cautery stick and leave for three days; and then apply a layer of butter bandage, allowing the wound to remain open as long as needed; continue with ointment treatment until it heals completely.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use very little of this cautery for the fear of his view, and there are few who use it; however, he states that this is a good cautery which one can bear with, and leaves where it happens.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The medical cauteries that burn involve making an instrument with interweaving parts where the edges descend to the entrance, made of steel or long iron, with two inches at its height and between each part, have a thickness as wide as one's thumb; they should be perfectly smooth on both sides and join together in this form.
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After placing on the hip bone of the lying patient against his side, quickly place your hand mostly onto the hip bone; then pour between the two circles of the hot ash heated in fire I pinch, and let it rest for one hour tightly, and allow the patient to endure the heat and burn.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For here it finds mastication also like that of fire; and when the mastication passes, remove your hand with the tool and lift the hip from the ashes gently. Let this rest for three days, and place butter on until that which is black from the charring is osteit; and let this sit for three days until putrefaction sets in. This would be the final aid after the ointment cure until it becomes sanez.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread up to the thigh or even to the leg, you should apply the hot tool similarly as you did on the hip, in equal measure; and this is the manner of hot application, and I have written it down or treated it for correcting medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take wood ashes and live lime, as much of one as of the other, grind them together, and mix them into a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	So if there is a small slit where a razor point can fit; and place it in that pot then another well weighted pot, and add wood ashes and lime to it until there's two inches above the powders. Make sure you hold this mixture firmly with your hand; and leave it like this until the ashes and debris or weight falls out of the bottom pot, then take all this mixture and pour it onto lime as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be like water and administered in the form of mixtures for medicine and other cauteries. For it performs work akin to fire, and also has utility with other medicines where one might cauterize well the hip in this way using honey, anacardium oil (a type of nut oil), lime and soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment where some men were cured of the pain in their hip and sciatic vein, and all the joints, and he says that no other treatment was done, and it was cured in one instance when this treatment had been performed. And they bathed themselves as Galen instructs below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And instruct them to prepare in this manner: take a portion of the litargire that is both fresh and dry, grind it finely with just a pinch of fat, and apply it onto the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain persists, then bind it. Leave it on for three hours until the affected area no longer feels the heat.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make them enter or bathe until their body becomes slightly warm, and have them rest in bed. The pain will disappear completely and they will be cured.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use such medicine cauteries, if this isn't after the removal of pus.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides states that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with donkey's dung grease, if it helps little; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take animal dung and mix it with old oil, and apply this mixture to the hollow located between the thumb at the ankle and the other one called the sole.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After taking dried donkey dung, hold it over fire until it turns into charcoal, and place it on the wool, and leave it until it is ashes; and repeat this process again, and do not stop doing so until you believe by reason that it will reach up to the hip, and that the pain will cease; and this way of cauterization is called "donkey dung cautery".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by impact or percussion or from too much evacuation, or due to similarity of cold substance spreaded, none of these appearances warrants cauterization, because that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary to follow this when the patient has been freed of infected pills or other similar symptoms, by applying it to the back where the pain is located, three lines marked with an X, and in each line from .v. to more cauterizations according to the virtue and quantity that the body can endure; and perform the cauterization according to the type of cauterization called "points"; and if you see fit, do 3 or 4 cauterizations at the midpoint of a standard cauterization like this:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often affects young children, and the signs of its beginning are that they become pale when they stand alone, and faint; and you find a swelling in the last spine of the back and an appearance that comes over other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and observe it being treated, if you apply the fire cautery according to this shape.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery pricks every part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, cauterize along the spine with the cautery touching two or three lines, and make the points close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure as long as it is clean according to what we have said, and beware that you do not apply the cautery on blisters which are in the vicinity of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	Of the pain in joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture spread throughout each limb, and when pain comes from the foot, which they call "gout" properly, and when it's due to cold reasons and its cures are made with medicines that can't heal it, then it should be treated using cauterization in this manner: make a hole inside the joint of the foot, and have olive oil cauterizations according to this shape:

And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, if you need to cauterize on each knee three or four across each part of the cautery; and if you need more, do more but don't remove your hand until the oil of the cure is completely burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, one administers the cautery as we have said in our chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if you treat him well and cleanse phlegm, he will recover with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of urine
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When dislocation occurs in the shoulder, and the muscles descend to the chest this is newly happening, it's necessary that when you see them being treated, do not disturb him during the day; and use things that relax his stomach, so that the intestines descend from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to shave his underbelly until the muscles are repaired, then bring him back to your fingers, and mark along the rupture above the bone of the elbow, and ensure every sign is like half a circle above the torso; then heat up the cautery which is formed thus:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and excretes gallstones.

Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your procedures are worthless.

Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to stand up, prepare him a well-made bandage and leave it on for another forty days; and have good rest, let him work little and guard against too much drinking and eating, and too loud shouting; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed.

de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen

li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for the sore by cautery

Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. quant li artere est copee	When the artery has been cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier. And still, when this happens to no one, if you hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press it very much until the skin is relieved under your finger, and no drop comes out; then light several small and large olive oil cauteries until they are all red. Then take .i., or large or small according to the wound and limb where the artery is located, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery there until the skin is completely cooled.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are off the fire, then take hastily another one of the cauteries that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bone is completely healed; and watch that you do not burn the nerve which lies beneath, and that no harm comes to the patient; and know that when a bone dislocates from an artery, one cannot properly heal it themselves when the artery is large, unless done through one of the four ways we have mentioned: by cautery, by extraction if it has not been treated, by strong thread binding or by medicine applied which has the power to heal blood; and then bind and keep it steady for the future.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the reattachment by tightly binding with cloths or by placing burning things on, or other similar actions, if it does not help then it likely won't.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have no tool or medicine at hand, then they should place their thumb on the wound of the vein as we said, and stretch it well until it is healed above the wound and above the vein; and do not move their finger, but often moisten it with cold water so that it stays very cold until the bone is frozen, swollen and healed. And prepare for cautery and medicines what needs to be done.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have spoken about the first chapter on all diseases where it is necessary to apply a heat cautery, or hot medicine, and their causes, instruments, and forms; and we placed that chapter up until the knee, and I will continue this chapter in the same manner so as to find what seems easier for whoever wishes to know.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this one, it is necessary that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first section about cauteries, which means greater caution must be exercised.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I urge you that you do not embark on folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	And none of the ways of people come to healing.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who are so troubled by their illness that they die lightly due to the foolishness they find in their disease, and from the great suffering of their wickedness; and one must have fear from these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of those I give you their meaning, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is insulting.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not right for you to agree with those who come to you in this manner, but place more consideration on your honor than on your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely of what you are certain, and of which you have knowledge; and use prediction and indication in healing the sick whose health has been restored. This will help you acquire good reputation, glory, and lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, our lords provide good understanding and righteousness to you, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of their hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter out of discussion by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter about the cauteries, which I discussed from the head up until the foot, because you will find it easier that which you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes very often to children at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the head of the child; and it happens in no other instance due to a reason that we know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and among all those I've observed, their death was hastened by it; for this reason, it seems to me that it is worth stopping the treatment with these remedies.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child of this kind where the shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day until it couldn't support more weight; and feared so much from the moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled beneath the bone within the socket, between the muscle and the bone. And the openings are such when the moisture is between the muscle and the bone, and the abscesses are small, that you make a wide cut in the head one groove; and be so long as two fingers, as long as the moisture runs; and here see the shape of the spathile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If there is more moisture, and the abscesses are larger, make two cuts in a cross-like manner, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the openings of the head's edges from each part, and water leaks when you press it inside with your hand, and this does not stop: then it is necessary that you make three cuts in the middle of the head in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after making the incision, remove all moisture completely outside.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After restraining the cuts from bandages and powders, and I place wine and oil, then let it be like this for five days; afterwards, release him, and treat the wound with dressings and ointments, and allow the head to heal equally, and finally have the patient eat dry meat of a bit of moist until the limb is strengthened and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the large opening of the abscess is, and gather water; for it is never in front, nor behind; neither to the right, nor to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut then the place where the abscess opens, and fill with water, and make a cut according to your ability; and be careful not to cut the artery; watch for blood flow, so that the patient dies from blood loss and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of cautery from fire, command the sick person to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it comes to any disease which is called "catarrh" in the eyes or at the bottom, and this sickness is old, and the treatment with medicine does not help, then the last resort therapy would be cautery using which one cuts off the two great arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	So then, when you see them recover, the patient must be placed upright; after that, rub with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, then remove the pus from his neck to all the cloths; then look where the vein is located, and examine both sides of the head after the ears, and then they have recovered somewhat; then mark the cheeks with an incision, then cleanse each side with a sharp needle of two parts, until the wound reaches up to the bone, and this should be done by going along the width of the neck.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, hold the spatula near the artery and vein above, cut also as two inches through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein has been severed, make sure to continue cutting upwards outward from there.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to pressure, it is necessary that you measure the size of the gap as three fingers wide, then gently push and press until you reach the bone; and what should be bled out is six parts per unit measurement, and by chance a little more or less according to how the patient can bear it and the resealing of the artery. Then look at the wound: if there remains just on point directly under the phalanx, then clean out any abscess that may have been left inside, then apply pressure evenly over the wound and secure it, applying ointment treatment until healed.
de emigrainne	"De emigrainne" translates to "from grain" or possibly referring to a process of sifting or removing grains. Without further context, it's challenging to provide an exact interpretation for this specific phrase within the medieval medical treatise. In general terms, in a medical setting, it could relate to procedures involving the removal of grains (such as pieces of gravel or sand) from bodily tissues or fluids.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old age approaches, and severe coughing occurs, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and elsewhere in the elderly body, as well as similar things, treatment is done using methods of medical cure and all this does not benefit it. Therefore, one should extract the arteries of the temples and apply a cautery, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The method of extracting them is that the patient feels beneath their temple hair, and listens to the artery emerging at the temple, as it opens well through its beat, responding only in some very cold individuals; if it responds, one should tighten a piece of cloth around its neck, then rub with a coarse cloth on one side, and raise above hot water until the artery becomes clearly visible. Then take the spatula which has this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you feel the artery, then lift it up with forceps and cut it well from each part; and if the artery is delicate, cut it at the tip of the little finger, then remove this from that part according to the size of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it's not cut, neither will escape all without pain.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And when the blood flows for 2.5 days, until it lasts for 3 days; and if the artery is large, you must tie it with two strong silk filaments in a double thread so that no rot occurs before the healing of the wound, nor does continuous bleeding happen; then cut away the excess between the two threads at that same moment, and then, if you see fit, cauterize it with a surgical cautery up to the bone until the shoulder is cut; this is the final work, if the patient doesn't have fever and has warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cauterization helps to finish off moisture issues: because in this case it provides greater assistance for moisture problems.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For when it's necessary for the extraction of arteries, fill the area with old cotton and place well-made cloths on top; and once you've freed them, apply dry medicines that create pus and cloths until there is no longer any moisture; and if you remove part of the artery as you are working on this task, quickly cauterize it with a cautery or use a glass container and squeeze your hand so that the artery dries off; and if you don't have a glass container available, fill the space with ice until the artery is frozen, then wash with cold water until it stops bleeding and ensure it's done correctly. The one that is wetter and more light during the extraction of an artery should be cauterized on this flat-ended cautery, but make sure the ends are well-spaced to last longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tight, they hold less of their heat.

des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure. Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called the old 'bruise cure', and if you treat someone with this illness, have them grow hair on their head or forehead, then make three cuts evenly across the forehead according to its length; and make one of the cuts as wide as two fingers along the entire front part down to a small notch, and the other two cuts at about two finger widths above the eyebrows, and be careful not to cut through arteries which are located above the eyebrows; keep your hand away from connecting parts of the jawbone, and each wound should cover an area as large as three fingers across; have a piece of sponge and cloth ready for wiping away any blood, then use the sharp tool made by dividing it into two parts like this:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is behind the temple up to the second incision; and scorch all the tissue that is between the two cuts all across the furrow above the bone, then make another cut from the halfway point of the incision up to the other cut, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you use a tool in the first incision that is called 'culetter', and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is hollow, not sharp, and this shape:

And pierce all the veins that descend from the head as far as possible with eyes until you reach the opening at the kidney, and then continue cutting halfway through the crack to another opening; and then remove equal blood, and drain the body for the taken blood; then place a piece of old cotton in each cut, and cover it with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil and basil, and make sure that abscesses do not occur; and on the third day loosen the stitch, and give it large baths of warm water, then apply the ointment of basil with oil rose, and other treatments for wounds until it heals.
dou reume des eulz	from the pus
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When it comes to sudden and customary cold sweats, you see the eyes reddened and small, and they weaken vision, and burned paper; and hair falls out, and one feels a fullness due to ague-like pain, and the patient sneezes; then recognize through these events that this substance and that fever come from multiple veins, and the treatment applied if it is so, involves this.
