And begin from the temple on the left to the temple on the right, and let the incision go down to the bone; and move your hand away from the temples' nerves that move during eating; and when the bone is uncovered, bleed it with a sponge until done, then cleanse inside the two lips of the incision and place old cotton, lin, then cover above with wet cloths in wine and oil; and keep yourself from pus. When removed, you should rub the bone as long as cartilage begins to form, then clean with desiccating things that shorten cartilage.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of clove oil, and make a plaster; and administer this plaster to the wounds to promote the appearance of char everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing.
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that enters into the ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, such as beans, peas; or flowing substance like water and sweat and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it discharges from the ear hole or in any other manner that does not fit to the ear, nor grows in the ear, then place the ear under the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it leaks any drop of purple oil or tallow oil, then proceed with extraction; and make him sneeze with common snuff, and block his nostrils when the sneezing comes on, and place pieces of cloth or wool inside the ear; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	It works many times with this treatment; and if it doesn't work, then he should proceed with the extraction using fine forceps, of which this is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the forceps, that's good; if not, proceed with extraction using a small delicate instrument of two halves. And if it doesn't jump out by that means, make an arachnid stick and press out its head or part of the stick near the ear strongly, and block the wick in the middle of the candle or rosemary to the extent that nothing can enter through the candlestick with the stick; then pull it forcefully as we have said; and if it does not work in this manner, take some glue from this substance and place a small instrument on it at a suitable point for doing so, and put a bit of cotton inside. Then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not heal from all these things that we have said, hurry to cut the ear in this way, allowing pus and blood to flow out, and spasms; and the manner of cutting is such that you first make a sinner on the cephalic side of the patient, and remove some of the blood according to its measure. Then let the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fatty area hanging down; and let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the bone. Then break the bone according to your strength, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and the cure as long as it is sound.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if they are grains and it is inflamed, administer an extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer one of these small incisions according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grains are wet due to the moisture in the ear, until you have removed many pieces; then extract with fine forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction goes smoothly.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In an earache therefore that causes weeping in the ear, then it is fitting for the patient to perform first-aid by making a hollow with some old cotton and letting the ear weep out.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And be still over that same ear or where the ache is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it leaps out through the sky, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	And if it doesn't go through the sky, take many stones according to the length of your finger and make them light, and heat them slightly on fire; and place one or more of these into their ear, and pull it out from under his feet from another side, and stick another stone against the stone in the ear; and continue doing this by passing the stone from one to another until all the ache comes out completely, and then if it leaps out completely. And if you see that, take a piece of rush, and insert one of your heads into the ear, and the other head with fire until the hardest part of the rush is burnt; then make this procedure with more rushes until all the ache comes out completely, just as we have said about the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of the beast, if it's of small size like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in division; but if it's of large size that can be felt, proceed with the extraction using forceps; this is the more gentle thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you apply treatments as we have described in division and distillations, if the cure does not help, you should look at the ear with the sun: if there is no worm visible, extract them using fine forceps; if it's not visible, take this form from here:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And make it narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most delicate thread into the ear according to the degree of suffering of the patient, then form it throughout the entire canal; do this repeatedly until all the liquid has come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, subdue inside the cotton canal as I have said in the case of stones; and if they do not protrude like we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective for worm expulsion; you will find these treatments in texts about distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, as shown here, follow this form just as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And whether it is made of silver or lead, make it narrow at the bottom with two small holes, and wide at the top for distillation; and to press internally in the middle of the distillation use one well-made tool made of lead specifically for this purpose. If you see a scraper and wrap cotton around the tip, place oil or juice into the cylinder, and whatever medicine you see inside it, let them be in the canal, then pour all the cotton with the scraper, press your hand appropriately until the oil is distilled or from the ear; and feel within, and make the distillations one small piece heated over fire like when you distill it into the ear. And remember not to let it get too cold, because the medicine would not be as good then.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a bit of ear wax; and this same thing happens with injuries or birth in the ear, causing eardrops that only come once inside the ear if they cannot be seen; and never do two drops of ear wax appear at once, you see them well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Thus, the one that comes inside if you cannot see it, is due to a blockage in various positions, and here what needs to be done becomes clear: you should place the ear near the sun; look inside: if you can see the plaque apparent, if the work has fully formed this pus-like substance from which we are speaking:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be so, cutting in front and behind it completely flat, so that it does not irritate the ear; if there is a plaque or bump from inside the ear or of the ear itself, if you have fine pincers, use them to carefully cut, until all the char has been removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the ointments are well applied in the ear, take a delicate thin tool and heat it slightly over the flame, then place it inside the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you notice the swelling that the ears feel irritated by touching them gently, ensure not to press on the nerves of the ear; then insert a tent into the ear according to its width, and add moistened Egyptian ointment in the ear.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Continue this for as many days as the wound is healing, or take a patch and moisten it with rose water, then sprinkle powdered vitriol over it. And if you see swelling in the ear, it should be that you remove the patch and apply another wetted patch made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling is removed; then treat it until it is well healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a cloth and wet it with cold water, then put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are similar to those used for distillations.
de la char des papieres	From the residue of paper
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	In the process of unfolding hairs when they are moist and drying, it is necessary to use tweezers and forceps on them. Take a small slice from their roots; then place under the glass tube.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if you do not remove the thorns, cauterize them with a thin round cautery iron. After incision, it's worth removing them; and they are often cut again, because nothing remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized by fire, those root parts burn and never return.
de la gresle	Regarding ice
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times papers come with some things that seem to crack due to their shape and hardness, and this is a disease called "hail", which is an assembly of large moisture gathered on and under the paper; the actions are as follows: take care if hail moves from one side to another, it's a simple matter to know; then make them wide, followed by scorching each part gently, then grasp them with forceps, and cut them.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you can't cut them without piercing the paper slightly, but don't harm the patient; and if it splits wide, if there's a seam in it, then treat until it heals completely; and if it is small, do not apply much force, because the ointment will heal it quickly and regenerate flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grains descend into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the grains on tweezers, cut and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it causes no harm; and when the grains are cut, remove the salty water, treat the surrounding area until the tissues regenerate; as long as the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the grease of the lumps
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Extraction is a grease that saturates the sheets of paper above, and this happens more with children than with adults, it hurts their eyes greatly, and it causes them to weep in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; and because of this, they lie upon their buttocks directly, and sleep there, and have their papers underneath their knees moist from the exudate which opens in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand onto it and feel the exinach between your fingers.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way to treat it is such that you have your patient's head in a healthy position. Then take one piece of linen cloth and set up as tent-like structure into a circular shape according to the amount of exinach present in each section, then place it on top; press with your hands from both sides so that all the exinach is gathered within the circle. Afterward, cut in the middle of the moisture, making a small slit not larger than the wound made when opening veins, and ensure that the linen reaches into the moisture completely. Then various sections of the exinach come out through this slit, resembling the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Pull out then, in one piece, the cloth padding between your fingers on the outside, and twist your hand to the right and left until it is spread; make sure not to block the slit, that you reach all the way into the moisture up to the eyes, do not hurt.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the exit does not open at the start of the incision, increase a bit the incision gently until it opens; then treat it as we have said, then moisten with bandages and water, place it on the wound, and apply binders.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who grind salt and place it to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then he should be treated as long as he is sane.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to cutting an abscess there, then a plaster treatment is applied until the wound heals.
des poilz des papieres	(of paper hairs)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hair grows in other than its natural place and ages, it harms the eyes, causing various diseases like familiar infections and paper weakening or scarring, as well as white discharges due to this cause; and one treats accordingly with four methods: either by combined fire cautery, or through ague medicine as described previously in the section on cautery, and is done through cutting and sewing, or through sutures, according to what I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the tip of the eyelid in your healthy state, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it flips properly, it's good; if not, sew one thread above through at all .i. and attach another thread over the entire sheet of paper, and then turn it with a sharp tool; then cut in the area under the paper, under the displaced hairs, from the major tear to the minor tear; then remove the thread, place a small cotton tent on top of the paper along with a piece of silk, and then sew an outline resembling a leaf, like the bay leaf, onto the paper. Yet it is necessary that the shape match the amount you see when lifting the lifted paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there is work that requires handling large quantities of paper according to the paper's softness; then have everything ready for applying a plaster until the wound heals. After that, make any necessary adjustments under the second line you've indicated and start from the broadest area moving towards the finer parts. And let one of the slits be near the natural hair growth lines as it expands like a root, then place an ounce at one of the two corners of the good side, then remove all the scorching, then join both sides with a single thread on a needle for all wool strands, and clean out any blood. Then allow the excess thread to hang loosely between the second line's stitches on anything that glues together, if you're able to do this; and if it is not possible, don't worry about it. Leave the stitch and threads until three days or four. Then treat the wound without a stitch using dried and tightening substances because the paper will heal in response to the pressure of the wound and the joining process, but stitches tend to be healed (as the old say), and this is work without fear; and there's another way: you should mark the paper with a design that resembles the leaves of myrtle as we've described, using three ounces cut according to the shape shown here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut the one that sits above evenly, according to this form:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the ability to hold the forceps, and the thing is not even, take a needle or let there be thread, then stick it in the middle of the figure; and stick another thread diagonally from the large incision, and the second thread diagonally from the small one. Then join the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin over which you have indicated, as we have recounted, then join the two edges of the wound by suture, and keep the cure until it is clean; and if pus comes to your incision, then soothe it with tallow and some soothing ointment; and every time that the paper hair changes: so you must use what we have said about cutting; but the stitch in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of canes follows this form: and you should convert the paper and cut it inside according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and also two fine threads each as long as the paper and as wide as its thickness; and pinch these two pieces together at half way from the paper of the eye, and hold tight the two canes from their ends shaped respectively; and leave them like this for a few days, and the skin that is constricted will soften and heal and recover, until it discharges through itself.

de la bowe de l’oil	From the field of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not due to water that has gathered in the ear, resembling falling water but it's not water; and the way of its appearance involves making the patient sit upright with their head straight, then hold the chin between your two hands, and move them until you see the water rise above your ears; then let it drain out, don't stop and clear away any light, observe the ear as usual; if it doesn't drain naturally, know that it's water, and if the draining from the water isn't prepared as we have described.

des aigues de l’oil	From tears of the eye

de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh around the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh around the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans. des apostemes des levres	from abscesses of lips

des sordens	Of cauteries made with fire, command the sick person to let their hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

Certain times, teeth are gathered together at the front of the mouth, between the gums and the inside of the mouth, where the skin is ugly and rough; and at other times teeth turn black, yellow, or have worms until corruption reaches the gum, causing them to stink. Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have large members that do not bend when being pulled, and be made of well-crafted iron, and have teeth for holding as needed.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary to place wet cotton soaked in butter around the wound for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the metal is heated, take and hold the pliers called "algiefri", which make the patient's bone look like a surgeon's tool; and they should be done in such a way that it resembles a file, this is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if they do not want to come out of all these nails, it is necessary that you reveal the flesh entirely along the root and place the tool called "althalus", which means palanchet, as its form is shown here:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is free and large enough so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, that's good; if not, use all the tools you have available, as their forms are shown here afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this tool which has two points, as its form is shown here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and there are other tools placed according to the order of teeth, and this tool that appears to be large tweezers, as its form is shown here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be it this instrument that cannot break it, and know that there are few instruments of teeth; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise surgeons themselves find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their operations and diseases indicate him, because there are parts of diseases for which old teachers did not teach an instrument due to the diversity of these ones and so they do not break from a fracture or of the other bones, or if it rots, then he searches among the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be them large and well holding for holding the bone that it does not escape but that you may hold and remove it; then restore its place with medicines fitting to this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, seek all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and the shape is ugly, especially in virgin girls, you should know if this tooth has been born after another tooth, and it is not straight in place, and one cannot polish or file it: then you must extract it; and if it adheres with a tooth, take this instrument as depicted here, which resembles two small beaks, and it should be made of sharpened iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the tooth is inserted gradually into one's hand due to its hardness and because you don't move others, and if it can be seen that we could grind it, then this tooth is ground with a single grinding wheel as it is formed:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And similarly to the file used for making needles; and grind the tooth gradually into one's hand lightly over time, so that it doesn't move until it cuts; then make it flat at the end with all nozzles, and if it is too sharp and it irritates the tongue, then you must grind off the roughness until it is even, so that it doesn't irritate the tongue or spoil speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth becomes loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front of the socket, by percussion or by striking it, and if the patient cannot press on this what he eats that it doesn't hurt, then they have been treated with medicines to reduce inflammation; but if it's not enough, you must restrict them with a gold thread because silver threads turn green and rot, whereas gold never changes; and choose the thread to be neither too thin nor too thick, depending on the space between the teeth. And if you see that the teeth are being pushed together, take the thread and place both ends of it inside the two healthy teeth, then insert the diseased tooth between the diseased teeth if there is one or more, until you feel comfortably against the healthy tooth from the other side; then redo the covering up to where you inserted it, and pull your hand gently and skillfully, until it doesn't move at all; and tie your thread around the root of the tooth so that it can't escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then bind the teeth with thread using tweezers, and assemble them, and place them between healthy tooth and gum, making sure not to hurt the tongue; then leave them this way as tightly as they can stay without causing pain. If they come loose or if threads get out, replace them with another thread; if it stays in and serves like that for its whole duration, and this is the arrangement of teeth and the location of the two healthy teeth and the two molar teeth as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth dislocates, if you put it back in its place, bit by bit, just as we have said; and don't interfere with anything that isn't careful and suffers, and not once does one make the shape of an ox bone tooth, and then place it at the spot where the defect is, and tighten it like what we've said, and stays and serves for so long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No part comes from under the tongue or is natural when one is born; or through accident of a stitched wound; and the operations are such that you work on the mouth in contact with the illness, have its head next to your healthy side, lift up the tongue; then bind the nervous cord as wide as possible until the tongue has been displaced from its place, if there is hardness or swelling, this means sudden healing, so pinch the hook and bind the wider one accordingly; and ensure that the cut doesn't go too far inward, because there's an artery underneath. And once completed, cool it with pink water or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and treat each night to prevent the teeth from sticking.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes out from this injury, place the glass tube on the wound; and if there's no bleeding, use slow fire cautery which is good for such injuries; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it's of color or black or hard, such that the patient doesn't feel it when touched, do not touch it for fear of gangrene; and if it turns yellow and shows pus, with moisture present, should you pull off the hook, cut out a thin incision from both sides, and remove it completely. And if the pus continues to come up through your apparatus, place vinegar over it until it's dried, then return to your operation while working with all your strength; then raise your head with cool water and other treatments until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	regarding throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No matter how many times phlegm enters the throat cavities which are called "godath", and they are properly known as the two amandeloids. When you treat them as we have said in the division, and if they don't heal, then be careful: If these are hard pus-filled lumps with a fine texture and colorless, do not touch them with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, for fear of causing blood to flow; but let it bleed until it stops, then you will remove it, or it might burst on its own. And if it has a white coloration inside and the root is delicate, prepare your instrument for extraction, but first check if the pus-filled lump has subsided and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	So have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his limbs should be in their normal position. And let him open his mouth and grip the surgeon's hands with them, pressing the tongue from all over the instrument; this is how it should look; and use silver or fine tin as sharp as knives for this purpose.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all of this instrument? And when you see pus, take the tincture and insert it into the almond, then pull it upwards more than you can; and remove nothing from the strings with this, then apply to the tool as described here, which seems like a strong force. And both the head is tied together, and one place another, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or arsenic:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool present, then use forceps, as depicted here:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make incisions on both sides, and on each side you name; when you have cut out one of the almonds, then cut the other according to that same manner, and after making the incision gargle the patient with hot, sharp water, and cold water too, and if bleeding starts, then gargle with hot water, or slices of cooked rhubarb, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then perform the cure until it is healthy; and in no case let other abscesses form in the throat than those two almonds, so cut them accordingly like the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, which is what we call the small abscess; and I had almost completely sealed off all of the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the obstructed passage, and she could not eat or drink, and died if she continued like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscesses had ascended so much that they had caused two rows of blisters under each nostril.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I immediately proceeded with haste, and removed one node of the lymph, then extracted this tendon outwards, taking away a large portion of the flesh; afterwards I made another incision in the other arm near the neck, and cut him open to make his mouth, pressing on his tongue as well. Afterward I inserted the node into the abscesses, cutting off some part, and only a little blood came out; henceforth it was unclogged removing the passageway of the throat in this manner; he began now drinking water and then wine, ceaselessly cutting at that wound for an extended period; and the pus recrystallized immediately filling up to such extent as I had drained out, until it became quite large; after which I stitched him up and cauterized inside his throat: thus he remained without growing larger. And left those parts, leaving only God's work to be done thereafter on him.
de l’uve	regarding the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it descends into the womb, and it inflates and becomes long, this is called 'perpendicular'. And if it's large and spherical, it's called 'the egg'.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the section, and if the treatment does not help, and you notice that the abscesses are calmed, and they are soft, then you should apply something to them; and the one which is round gathered together and isn't long; and it is bloody or has a red color or is black, so you should avoid making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the method that I have described in regards to its size and length, you should have the patient face the sun, and press their tongue with the tool we previously mentioned. Then insert the thimble into the womb, pull it towards you, and apply pressure using the two instruments I've mentioned for cutting the two almond-sized lumps during the incision of the two almond-sized masses.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not carry out more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit; because if you do so much, it will injure the voice and speech. And after cutting, use what we have said about cutting in chapter II of the almond, and treat until she is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patients have fear about cutting, it is necessary that you apply means to their sense of fear in the process of cautery.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The way of cautery involves using an active instrument.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patients make their head touch your health, and then press their tongue to the instrument we mentioned or chapter of cautery, and mix it with lively hot water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the force of this tool, as described below:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let my head have a hair or where I put the medicine, like the movements of a spoon, and place the tool completely with the medicine over the eye socket; and the patient should remain stationary on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine inside, without it descending to the throat or causing irritation; then keep your hand on the medicine and press it over the eye socket for about half an hour, until you see it absorb and the medicine's impacts are relieved; if you notice this, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the tool completely on the cotton in the wax, until the cotton dries up on the eye socket; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry off, and clean after four or five days. And if you need to reapply the medicine cautery, then do so, and afterwards, wipe around the eye socket with cotton dipped in butter, cleaning that area where there's leftover medicine; rinse with cold water and perform gargling until it is fully healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or the cautery; if it is treated with fumigation like this method, take calamus and juniper and oregano and rue and chamomile and clover and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them into one pot, and put water in it, and let it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot have one tool knife according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it's silver or arsenic, and whether one of the shoulder bones put in the mouth to the patient until the vapor rises into the lung by the nose, until the lung is damaged; after that you often repeat this, until the lung dries out, and remember not to do this at the beginning of the eruption of a pus lump, because many things occur; and do not do this treatment until it's nearing the end of the pus lump eruption.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a piece of wood and place an eggshell inside the patient's mouth, so that the patient's mouth is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow steam to burden the mouth, and it is a good treatment combined with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it happens in the throat bone or spine of fish, where nothing occurs; if therefore you are able to do so, then pull out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the tool, so that you see the thing move; and whatever does not open up and is stuck in the throat, it's necessary for you to make the patient vomit like this until the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing is expelled due to vomiting; or if a piece of sponge, navel, lettuce root, or one piece of dry bread is ingested by the mucus. And tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it afterwards; and when it comes up at the head, if it clears away, and then pull out forcefully; and if it doesn't come out from what we have said, then take one tool of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And prepare the instruments to the throat so that they can enter more lightly into the mouth, and have the head lifted up high above it; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything goes wrong or pushes the bone inside; and move so that the patient pushes the instrument in its entirety equally until she does it forcefully, as long as it is pushed forcefully.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the saliva of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no way to treat the blood withouts as I've mentioned in division by medicine treatment; and when this does not help, then look inside the patient's throat at noon, then press their tongue with the tool that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood, guide it out with every small fraction, or with fine tweezers that suffice for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this doesn't work, take a piece of a hair and push it into the throat of the patient, then remove or stop the bleeding with the end of the hair by twisting it. And do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you dye the patient's body with water throughout the day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full cups of cold water and work in the mouth, then pour it down without letting them swallow, and move it often with their hand. And as soon as they feel the water in their blood, they will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she does not vomit as we have said, then smoke the patient with asafetida, using the tool I mentioned for ophthalmic fumigation. Do this many times, because it will come out without discomfort.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of fumigation is this: you take the pot where there are glowing coals and place it under a cover with an opening in the middle. In that space, have the patient's head at the tip of the tool; then pour your fumigation over it, and make the patient put the tip of the stick into his mouth, closing it so no smoke can escape but goes until near the nostrils; and from there comes the fluid now, if it doesn't come out, start the fumigation multiple times; and let the patient thirst, consume salty things and alike, and do not drink water; then the task becomes for this manner to allow it to exit through this process.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to treat the mucus is such that when one can see it, it resembles curved tweezers meant to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has the texture of steel, so whatever she takes doesn't let go; here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	This chapter deals with abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are various types of abscess discharges, as memory suggests from one to another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; and there are two ways, the first being in its own form, and concerning the one which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those limbs they are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those in the foundation, and the abscesses of the internal body are different from those that come into joints, and each has its judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if with abscesses one must not pierce until the wound dies according to its completion; and for those that should be pierced when they are swollen and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses located at joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	And when abscesses are located at joints, and they remain swollen internally, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint have become corrupt, which is a cause of constriction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For the abscess is beneath the main limb, and if you delay the incision until it's dead, it will harm the main limb. Or if it's beneath the base, if you pierce it or in any way cause its death; you should not perforate a blood clot without digestion completed, unless that which is beneath the base would rot completely, and be deep inside, then causing a fistula; and cannot heal in great span.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be that you know the time for piercing the abscess which is done according to its maturation, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and from the movement and firmness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it must be that you place the piercing area as close or as far as needed from the abscess, and where it opens; and make the piercing at a point along the length of the body, and whether it is in the hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and all equal areas or places without fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the fatty part of the body, it is right to wait until digestion has been completed before making an incision, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	But if you pierce it before that point, it will spread the venom throughout the body and fill with maggots; and may硬化 his skin and lower parts of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if in any abscesses they pierce according to the breadth of the body, as per what the body requires for its members.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it should be that you introduce small punctures, small openings; and for large abscesses, large canals, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses or if it's necessary to use a knife and cover; when they have become as thin as a piece of cloth, and are softened, then you should do so like how one does with milk bottles: and for those that are split into three angles, and for those where one covers them just like the leaves of myrtle, such as abscesses from angles; and for those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar shapes are covered.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, such as abscesses superficially placed, it is necessary that you puncture them completely; and when the abscesses are large, and contain much pus, and you puncture them, if you do not drain all of the pus at once, but instead only part of it; then apply pressure on the abscess until the other side drains, then leave no thing inside immediately afterwards; repeat this process step by step with each increasing size, until all of the pus is drained; even when the pus is weak or when pregnant women are treated, or in young children, or in old sickly individuals.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when the attempt shakes every time with the expulsion of pus, perhaps causing death to the patient, and you do not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter by great caution, and when you have punctured your abscess, if the wound appears, observe if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a simple puncture scar, then apply strips of linen or old cotton; and for large abscesses, with many pus discharges, then you must press each one with a strip so that they stick to each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and left it sutured together, then fill it with old cotton or wool from linen without moisture, and keep it in place until midday; then remove it, and apply ointment until it heals properly.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding at your operation site, apply cold water gently and easily, and moisten the cloth, then place it on the affected area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then manage and treat it effectively, and apply the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it's caused by ice or if the place of your wound or abscess is very nervous, it's necessary that you put wet cloths soaked in wine and oil on the affected area; and if it's skin irritation, and the part is swollen, it's advisable to cover with cloths moistened in water and oil, or wine and cold oil until the third day as we have said; and then remove the wound dressing, clean it, and apply treatment as required, until it heals properly.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatments of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and here begins the chapter.
des soros	of the wounds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Tiny abscesses come from the head, and they are in the form that we find them on cloths, like under a gooseberry's skin, and there are many that resemble these.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are those that are fat and such where there is moisture as with warts; and there are some that are hard like stones to the cutter, and there is no doubt that the blood artery does not do otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the procedures of cutting are such that you must test with all the instrument which is called "intromission", from which the following form comes, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if you make the incision too long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And repeat the cotton application as before, for the second day and the third day too, until you know for sure that it does not stay wet overnight. Then apply ointment to the wound in what seems appropriate, while it is still clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess persists with thick pus, then follow this form of extraction, longitudinally. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And similarly, treat if it's tubercular, and cut and cure as I have instructed you to.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when it comes to cutting on the tubercular abscess and moist area, it's easier because they contain less blood.

And if in any of these abscesses or head, there is no moisture, and among the old woman's abscesses that I observed or heads; and found the abscess like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not be broken; and even if one had pierced it, one would have made just as good a wound as with a stone.

In other abscesses or head, there are those that come from the heads of children and the roots of the ears. des scrophules	regarding the treatment of scrophula

Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and around the armpits, and in the throat, and never come to any other part or corner, they are soft and are intertwined with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scab is properly within its coat, as the nut and the abscess on the head, as we have said; and the appearance of these scabs are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are tele's that contain moisture, and some that don't want to comply with health.
