In those where you see good arrangement at the stove, and it resembles the color of the flesh, mute from each part and is neither too close to the throat nor near the artery or in the duct, and is not deep; then it should be that you cover it above, and scorch each part, and extend the two lips of the earlobe if you need to, as we have said for abscesses on the head; and cut slowly and slowly, and make sure you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and there is no scraping or digging, that your hands don't escape, and don't look too far ahead, so that you don't cover more than what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery and it doesn't allow opening, then apply vitriol or any powders that stop blood flow in the wound, and hold the wound back. Leave it like this until the abscess subsides, and until the wound becomes soft, and it begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood has stopped, return to your task as long as you are completing it; then according to your skill test if there are any small spots remaining, remove and clean them if they do.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the spot, it's not right to cut that spot from its root. Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	And it is necessary that you cut to reach the root of it, and draw out pus, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those pimples that have excess, pierce them where they open; and pierce it like the one mentioned before, hanging down, then apply ointments and similar things to it, so that it decays what is inside; and when the wound is well cleaned, then apply ointment over flesh until it becomes healthy.
de squinance	Regarding squint,
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke of the art of gullet surgery; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is written down from their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the incision in the throat referred to as "epiglottis" be made; and one should not try this technique because all the vessels and the heart are close to these who have a large amount of mucus either in their mouth or in the throat or near two almond glands.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	So when we wish to cut the epiglottis, we should make cuts across three or four small slits through it, between the two circles or according to the size of the slit, not penetrating into the cartilage; and these cuts are suitable for dividing the epiglottis so that there is no flesh left behind, and the vessels are long enough without obstruction.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are afraid, it is necessary for them to extend the skin of the throat throughout the inch, then cut the keur until it comes to the cheneil; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any thing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the flow of the cheneil's stream which jumps out through the opening in the part that was broken, and due to the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed from which one doubts strangulation, gather together the two lips of the wound neatly, and across the entire cut without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause growth until it is clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim, instruct that this should be done until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient's life judged to be at an end, and when there is no further improvement.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut on the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe normally anymore and they are breathing through the wound. This way, you guard against death. And according to the old men's command, it is necessary to keep the wound open until the disease passes away from the body; it usually takes 3 days or 4. Then they commanded to stitch up the wound and clean it, as long as it was being treated properly. And I will tell you what I have observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife and stabbed it in her throat, cutting part of the windpipe. And I was summoned to treat her, finding her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and indeed, it wasn't accompanied by a severed artery or exit route other than the throat, and the veins bled through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed quickly to treat the wound and cleaned it as she recovered. To the maiden, I simply needed her to regain her voice which was burned, and she returned to herself afterwards. This is why I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	In the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "throat hernia," and they are large lumps of a dark purple color, occurring often in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; or natural does not have an organ.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidents occur in two ways, with one resembling fat under our skin, and the other way resembling an abscess that comes from within us, through arteries. There is fear here and it's not appropriate to perform open surgery unless for something small; you should use your skill and search carefully everywhere: if you find it similarly to fatty tissue that can't reach any vein, then cut it out like one cuts fat under the skin, remove it all parts of its cover, if there are any; thoroughly search everywhere and treat appropriately until it is completely healed.
des nous	from the bones
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways there are to do this, so I will state all similarities; thus it befits me to explain every distinction that exists between us and the outcome.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the body's flushes have passed and putrefaction has occurred; then, the fever and heat settle.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one [here referring to a newborn], there is no heat or fever or pain, and contains its sap, which is its own sac and lies within the body's color, and begins also like a bird, and grows large; and are according to two appearances, oily or moist, and many of colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of new injuries, it is necessary that you first inspect and inquire about all the tool which is called 'the adjuster', according to its shape or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of incision for our pus is that you seek to make it even more moist than you find within the pus, and twist your fingers slowly, until you know that the instruments have reached the core, then according to the size of the pus; then extract the central part, and take care not to rupture it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture is the cause of the fire cautery, as long as it's there and in whatever form it exists, if you apply it just like I have explained for other abscesses; and if afterward no further inflammation comes from inside, understand that the pus was oily, so cut open accordingly, then do as follows - pinch the area, lightly scrape it from all sides, make sure to cover where the material resides underneath. And if you can't extract it whole, remove in pieces ensuring nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if nothing is left behind, it will reoccur many times; and even if a little remains, if it does not bother you, apply powders that are corrosive to the wound and hold it in place, and put on soothing substances for an abscess to heal. Continue various treatments until it heals properly. And should there be a large amount left over from the wound, cut out two layers of the tissue around the abscess; then treat the area where it is festering.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too large or another condition requires urgency and you need to treat it with vinegar poultice, let it remain for one or two days or three, until the wound discharges pus, then rest in hot blood; afterwards return to treating where he has been exposed to the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the entomissoirs instruments, and they come in three ways: large, medium, and small. And among them there are three quarters which are called 'albaret', and one that is called 'breb'. There are also similarly shaped as needles used to remove warts, made from citrine quartz, or iron, or silver. The yellow ones are considered more effective than black cork for surrounding fistula ulcers. They come in three shapes: large, medium, and small, depending on the width of the grooves.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the incisions are similar to mowing blades, as you see here: large, medium, and small. There are also oncine instruments that have two grooves in three ways; there are ones with three grooves, which are also available in three forms; there are those with two grooves, and oncines with just one groove, all of these are available in three shapes; all these are necessary according to their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of this part where one makes the cut is done, and among those who do not cut by force from both sides, they blister their skin; because here there's no cutting into the vein or nerve. And these introducers are used in gloves so that the patient does not notice during abscess opening. They come in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses no force but in the chest muscles, such as legs, arms, nipples, and underbodies, and similarly other parts; and one always makes another smaller tool resembling cutters of artisans, according to this shape where one stops bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed in the healthy part of the body, at the junctions of veins and arteries, and never according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	None of the men's nipples swell when they begin to become corrupted, until they look like female nipples; and remain swollen and bloated, and whoever wants to cure them should do so according to this line’s instruction from .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scorch the fat and cover the wound with medicine that stimulates flesh growth. Then join the two edges of the wound for suturing, and treat it until it heals; and if the nipple sags downwards due to its size, and is flattened because of its grandeur as in women, then cut it into two halves above, through two semblance of cracks; from which one holds onto the other at the end of each half, so that the larger line contains the smaller along this form, from this line .b. up until the line .g.; then scorch the skin between the two edges and remove the fat. And do as we have said about suturing and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment, until it heals; and if it does not heal or if the incision is not completely made because the patient cannot rest, or due to blood discharge, then you must fill the wound with moist cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it till it starts healing removing the cotton and fat, then treat it until it fully heals.
des apostemes des asselles	from abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that originate in the armpits are manners of hard scrofulas where there are nodes, and if there are any containing moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should have their limbs cut according to this form, from the line .b. up to the line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has drained out, fill the wound with old cotton and let it be for another day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses resemble scrofula sores, make incisions as we have said in cuts for scrofula sores, and if the wound is filled with pus, apply a cautery as we have said previously.
de la routure de l’artere	regarding the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut and the skin above it is sewn together, many times there are discharges (of pus), and similarly this happens with veins and abscesses; and if one knows this when it's because of the artery, then these discharges are long and deep; and when you feel them with your fingers, they feel like constriction; and when it's due to a vein, there is an opening that appears after. And cutting such an incision is foolishness, and even more so when it's over joints and muscles and under the collarbone and in other parts of the body where it's very large, and is extremely large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid iron treatment. One must also avoid it for the head, and for those with swollen arteries above the skin, incisions are made right across them. Then work the size in inches, and carefully separate the artery from the membranes until it's fully uncovered; then stick an instrument beneath the skin all along its length, and make a hole to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places as instructed in the extraction of two arteries in temples. Then pull out the middle part between the two threads with any intervening material until the discharge is released and you can remove it; then treat this area with antiseptic ointment until it heals properly; and if the discharge is due to a vein, it's wise that you dab the part of the pus that you can touch on all your skin, then stick an needle beneath the one hand-held piece and make another hole, ensuring there are two threads so you can pull them from both sides; then bind this discharge in the way I've instructed before, or with a single stitch on either side using silk thread. And if you doubt whether the thread will pass through, insert another needle all along the length of the pus-filled area at the opening of the first needle and bind it together in three places; then trim off the excess until everything is cut away, then trim properly leaving what's bound; then place a moist dressing with wine and oil on this area, then treat it with antiseptic and ointment treatments until it heals fully.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also like abscesses appearing in arteries and veins, they appear on nerves when they are cut or due to too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often happens with shoulders and elbows and in all places where there are joints, and it is the pain from abscesses, and their color seems like the color of flesh, and is found in many positions without pain; and when they are tightened, the patient feels pain, but not just throughout the body, but inside the bone; and moves well in all directions, neither forward nor backward, neither down nor up, and one who is jointed should not be covered with iron: by chance there would be a contraction; and that which is on head or forehead makes the skin shiny.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscesses are small, and you have tweezers, then clamp them at their root; and if they are large, suspend them from the wrist, and scrape, then remove the bone, stitch up the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Of large boils hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	In no parts of the body except the belly and nowhere else, there is a disease which is named "fungus" by analogy with these things, and it has delicate roots, and big knots; and there are both small ones and very large; and I knew one person who had two bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference between them, they were white, and had small roots, and were deeply split, and corroded almost instantly due to moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied them and found in the first one eighteen ounces weighing, and in the other six, and the cuts from the incision are such that if you look, the skin is moist and the color of the wound is white and moist with a delicate root; if it is cut into a large pustule, and let the fire cautery be upon your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For when the surgeon comes often there are too great bleedings, and if it does not stop, then you must quickly use the cautery; and if you see the patient is frightened and full of fear from the cut of the iron, take a well made thread of linen, tie the knot as we have said, and leave it two days; then tighten, and do not cease pulling the linen thread until it fits the knot, and no effort is required; and if the roots are thick, it causes fear to bleed even for the belly, but you can bleed half well then cauterize so that it does not reappear; then treat the wound, and ensure you do not bleed the part that is of a red color and poor sense and milk appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess, and I will come to the treatment of gangrene next.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the bladder burns
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	When it appears on the wound or the crack in the syphilitic sore, and it is on the belly and there are some ulcers, as happens in other cuts, or blood that comes from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned previously, or due to windiness; and if it's through the cut of the syphilis and by the exit of the pus, then it has a color similar to the redness of the abscess, and is a light thing without pain, and opens up from various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it's due to the exit of an intestinal tract, then it is more varied. And when one presses it with their fingers, it returns and then comes back again, and by chance gets stuck, and enlarges quite a bit at the entry from the bath and through strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's due to moisture, this is a small thing, and opens well when you press on it with your hand, nor does it resist; and if it's due to blood, you open by these signs large and hard abscesses, and are located according to their quantity; and if it's due to winds (windiness), it is difficult in the field, and the openings are that you look at its appearance being for the blood of an artery, or of a vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary that you allow the treatment to proceed.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in such matters, as I have explained or outlined in the chapter on abscesses, concerning arteries and veins.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if its appearance is like that of an intestine or the gallbladder, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to apply a cautery to their oil, and have it extended completely straight. Then, sign and let the oil flow all around the opening; then direct them to do so with moderation in your hands, then go inside the area where you indicated and extend the abscess half way up on the large uncus; then bind that part of the abscess with a strong thread or a firm silk string, ensuring it is securely tied. Then, extend the other half of the abscess out over this binding, and place your index finger near the intestine; if you find it caught by the binding, loosen it, and pull the intestine up to the exit from the belly; and if you find the gallbladder, take hold of its uncus and remove any excess. And should the artery or vein oppose, enter them fully, then return to your work and take two needles, and fix their threads at both ends as you pierced crosswise before making a hole; then pinch out the abscess in three stages over these needles, and if it appears, remove the needles and allow the area to heal, letting the dead tissue decompose on its own; or cut it when it becomes thin and cooked, then treat the area as necessary, apply oil to the abscess like we have instructed. And remove any blood or moisture you find, then treat the area according to need, and sew up the opening.

Then join the two breasts with a good double thread, heat one end of the moisture on fire; then insert the head of the irrigating tool into the penis, and pull your hand over the bladder until all the moisture has passed, so that the patient feels it come into the bladder; and if you can't get the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, make a circle with it, pierce it roundly from edge to edge. Then join this piece in two parts tightly with the thread, form it like a girdle by joining them together as one would fasten a buckle, put inside what you see of moisture and water, tie it into the tool; do this just as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until all the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have spoken of the methods for stone division and extraction in medicine; we also spoke about the differences between stones that pass through urine and all signs, and which stones require size reduction; in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will openly and briefly tell you this.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones that get stuck in the bladder often occur more in children, and this is a sign that an infection has traveled from the bladder like an infection in its subtlety; and they often pass urine, and irritate the patient's penis, and it swells many times, and then returns; and at some of these infections there are stones; and until about four years old, children have easy recovery, but it is quite painful for the elderly, and occurs halfway between childhood and old age; and stone treatment is easier for those who have large stones compared to those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient by laxation, in order to remove all the bile that is within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	Because it clogs up every time when trying to cut into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take hold of the patient by their limbs, and lay them down and move them backward, so that the stone descends to the bladder's outlet, and exits none from its upper part; then have them sit between your hands prepared, and their hands under their thighs, so that the bladder is fully tilted downward; then touch it and feel inside; if you sense the stone in the space, now quickly cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it doesn't pass upon gentle touch everywhere, moisten your index finger of the left hand with your hand's oil, if the patient is young or old; and press into its base, and feel inside for the stone, and when you sense it on your finger, remove it from the opening of the bladder; then press down onto that finger, and force out what you see cut outward.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the surgeon to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to extend his right hand upwards above the penis, and have his left hand hold the skin over the penis in the place where the cut should be made; then he cuts out the stone, this is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make the space between those who are within the knees and the foundation, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh; and be upright on the stone, and have your feet either on the base or against the wall, and have the height so that it goes through if it is wide outside and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance press on the foot which is on the foundation, making it jump out without effort; know that there are parts of stone where angles, edges: it hurts when trying to escape; and there are parts at the bottom, resembling a nut, and round-shaped, from which the exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And in those parts that have angles and edges, make the opening larger; if it doesn't jump out, then you should use the tongs which are like a file at their tip to force out the stone so it doesn't escape. Or you can push from below with a fine curved tool at its tip; and if you cannot work this way, simply widen a little more of that part slightly bent inward. And if you don't manage to craft it this way, make it wider but not too close to the skin edge; and if you leave it open, force it out with vinegar; and if there are more stones, push the larger one first at the opening of the bladder, then work upward, then apply pressure forcefully, and do the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then it would suit to let her out, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: or he dies, or his urine comes out immediately while his legs cannot be sewn; but still try to drain or crush him with tongs, as long as you pull him piece by piece. And when you have completed your work, cover the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood sap, then compress it, and pour oil and vinegar over a cloth on top of it, or oil and rose water and cold water to cool the pus; then bandage the patient back onto his leg, and do not remove the stitches until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove the bandage, wash it thoroughly with water and wine vinegar, then apply a diaper ointment and basil ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if pus and corrosion enter the wound and clotting occurs in the bladder, and if this retains urine, which is known to occur in such a way that without jumping with urine: then you must apply force in the wound, remove that blood, because if it remains, it corrodes the bladder and rots it; then wash the wound with water and salt and vinegar, and help him in all ways that you know how until he is healed. And when treating him, you should tie his two legs together, and gather the medicines on top of the leg.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is located where the penis leads, and implanted within, and urine cannot escape; when you treat as I have described, that you cut multiple times, and allow for some loss due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I already know this experience like this.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron branch according to this form, and have it pierced at three points on each side.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take thread and tie it around the penis near the stone, so that it cannot return to the bladder. Then guide the needle into the penis gently until it reaches the stone; and move the needle with your hand inside the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side. If urine begins to come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone inside the penis.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken, and urine starts flowing, and the pain stops; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie the thread around the stone and another above it. Then have the penis be in place under the stone between the two threads, then pull strongly on it, and remove the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood from the wound; and treat until it is healthy.
de la piere des femmes	From the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that a stone becomes embedded in women, and if it occurs once, the cure is difficult, and must be done for three reasons: one, perhaps the woman is a virgin; and second, no one can find a woman who knows how to expose her eyes, even when she is pure.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third method is such that if you happen to not find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone within a woman is further inward than the stone within a man, so it requires a deeper incision, and there's great fear involved. And should necessity arise from this, then it befits you to seek out one who knows their trade well, and place your hand firmly on them; if you don't find such one, don't hesitate to consult a more subtle surgeon; and present someone who is skilled in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of this art, and command her to do what you are instructed about stone probing; and watch very well if that woman is a virgin: then it befits for him to stick his finger into its place, seeking out the stone; and should she find it, compel it from her finger hole, and instruct her to press her left hand onto her bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she should move it from side to side at the entry of the bladder until below, as far as to her thigh's root; then cut on the bone where the thigh meets the knee in the middle of the joint, where the bone is more evident and you feel the bone in that part; and do not move your hand over the bone above or below, make a cut at the first small size; then push out the rib in this size, if you feel the bone increase the wound until the bone can exit forcefully, and know there are many types of stones: this is to say, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those with edges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you understand the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it doesn't weaken him, place vitriol on the wound and hold it for an hour until the pain subsides; then return to your work, as long as the stone is strong, and prepare the tools I instructed you about in removing stones at home so they may assist you with your task. And if it doesn't weaken him, and that's due to severed artery, place powder on the wound and apply slices of leather or bandages, and don't repeat this process again, let the stone remain without trying to remove it for fear of injuring the patient; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has calmed down and the limbs are restored, then return to your work while the stone is hard.
de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Gelatinous growth is nothing else than a collection of moisture or white jelly, which resides in the sack of the kidneys, containing the egg; and it's called "jelly", and once it properly sits in the fabric of the egg if we believe there's another one; and this is the skin between the white jelly that we've mentioned; and this doesn't have a hole.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this gelatinous growth is due to weakness that affects the kidneys, and spreads that substance.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And never does this come from percussion on the kidneys, and this moisture takes many colors: or it's declining color to jaundice, or it's without redness, or black, or aqueous white, and this happens more often; and these are signs to recognize this assembly, because if it is white like we have said, then it's an abscess with pus, lasting as long as the figure of an egg, and not opening in the kidneys, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper tissue, then it's an abscess containing part of the egg, and because of this we think it's another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the kidneys and the white one, you will feel it well; therefore when you see to know the color of the moisture, test thoroughly across its entire area for the shape as shown.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Following then those who come after the preparatory step, judge by what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it must be treated with the best knowledge and power of one's ability and the replenishment of their body; then sit upon their back on something slightly raised, and set mounds under them with cloth. Then sit to their left, and command the minister to sit at their right, stretching the member towards one of the two ribs close to the armpit region; then take the spit iron, and cut through the skin along the length until beneath the knife, let there be a straight cut through the skin up till the white fat, and carefully shave it off. Then pierce the fat thoroughly with water at its deepest point, remove all of the water, and afterwards insert the needles, extend the fat upwards; do not touch the rib region but only allow the fat to remain; carve completely or in parts the flank underneath them precisely, if you don't carve it carefully enough then it will result in water again; should the chicken jump back into your work before finishing the fat section, reset it back in place once you have completed the work of the fat; then join the two layers at the rib region with one stitch, then treat it as any other wound until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit. Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the wound is divided into two parts together, know that these are two branches; so treat the other part in the same way as you treated the first equally. de l’aposteme des coions	Regarding the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in this part of the branch there is much fear for several reasons, which leads me to believe it's better not to use it; and I will tell you the action and similar aspects of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	So I say that many abscesses come from wounds or bites, and similarly in women; it's through certain cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know about the sour and feverish malaise which spreads among cattle or by percussion; and it's the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; there isn't any pain, and it's a pus-filled abscess; sometimes you might find hard, gravel-like abscesses with an off-color, and it never comes from a blood vessel, or swells up from veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches. des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that bleeding and sourness, when they occur through the anus, do not appear by smell, only is their treatment with iron indicates them.

des apostemes de la marris	The treatments for abscesses of the arm
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.
