Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary for me to describe this pus ball that comes in the marris, which is not among the pus balls that swell; and if you wish to understand how it occurs through iron means, then observe if the pus ball is hot and at its beginning of arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So don't rush to pierce it immediately, but let it die until the pain subsides; and then have the patient sit on a chair with two small seats where they lean, supporting their back and bringing together their feet towards the parts beneath the leg; and spread his legs wide, place his arms under his knees, tie them well in one good bandage; then push the stomach towards the right side of the ribcage, and adjust the tool used on the marris opening, which comes next with its shape. It is necessary that when you see this tool adjusted for use, make your first cut in this way to know the depth of the marris, so that what enters inside the tool does not go too deep than it should, and does not injure the patient; and if the tools are larger, then cover the depth of the marris with cloths, so that the tools do not bother them. It is necessary for him to place the funnel of the tool above, and mark the tool.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and one lets it drain with gentle hand, you should cover its head or the lip's cut end. And once the wound is empty, you should insert wet bandages soaked in rose oil or pure green oil into the wound; place them at the bottom of the wound under the marrons (a type of herb), and on top with a clean linen cloth moistened either with water cooked with malves or with water and long roots of lilies and aristolochia cooked up. Then after two days, apply an ointment fitting for this purpose until it heals; do not ever lift the marrons or the wound through vinegar and honey rinses, then again with water and cooked lily and aristolochia roots before applying the ointment. After that, revive them with the healing balm.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed on the marron herb, you should avoid heating with iron, but treat it as we have instructed in the previous section.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Profession comes first in knowing the figure of natural birth and its signs. When you see a woman's body ready for delivery, wanting to smell the amniotic fluid: then the baby is about to be born swiftly; this indicates that the birth proceeds naturally according to its inherent form, and issues forth from his head, followed by his secondaries with him; when you see these signs, gently pressing her abdomen is appropriate, so that the baby comes out quickly; for when it descends from its head, its secondaries come along with it, being cleansed of excess through good hygiene practices; anything else not following this manner does not occur naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes from no other place but his feet, or to the body or shoulder, and hands; or it may come near his belly or groin, turning by chance down his neck, or through other malevolent postures; for which reason, in this matter, she must be wise and subtle about these things, and be aware of deception and error. And I will show you all the positions on how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child descends through its head in natural birth, and the woman experiences severe pain during labor, and her strength is weak, she should sit on a chair or have women hold her; then rise from her nature with something cooked from fenugreek, and then place the midwife between her hands with a small spatula which has this form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut the second part, and remove up to his moisture which is inside until it's out; and pull on the woman's belly as the child descends, if it doesn't descend, then you must administer castor oil with fenugreek juice to the woman. Then have her drink and sneeze with mustard, and keep her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come forth.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if they come out with both hands, you should gently push them in and out; and if they cannot enter, put the woman on a seat, lift her feet upwards; then pull down the seat to the ground, and shave the woman so she does not defecate during delivery; and if neither hands nor child can enter, and the baby has died, you should use the hand that was prepared beforehand, and extract the child, and push them out evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the birth of the child above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes near its feet, it is what suits to thrust upwards; and then turn little by little, until it becomes even; then stretch out its legs gradually.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can it jump up to the thighs, if you order it to take hold, and make it snort with discomfort; if it jumps further, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, if one makes it move little by little, until it is according to the natural form.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be slightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it doesn't jump as we have done, say take a muscillaige of height, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in the mortar; and put this mixture inside and outside the ointment on her body, then make her sit in hot water until under her ribs; and when she is moistened underneath, make her wear a myrrh necklace, and place it upon her, and let her rest for an hour; then have her sit on the stool, then have her snort and restrain her mouth and nose, and gently rub her stomach, because the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the child's position on its knees.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child arrives in this form, if you place his hands gently and gradually; then be attentive on his neck, and let him hang from his head downwards, and lie sideways on the bed; and bend his hands gently and gradually, and then hold his hands on his belly, and remove the pillows underneath until she is hanging downwards; and if the child does not jump, take her feet and push forcefully, then push towards his belly, then I thrust my hands; and pull out the baby gently; and command the woman to pray as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	From the birth of the child that comes out with one hand on the way,
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to try to bring back the hand: if you cannot bring it back, then make the woman stand up and walk. If she can't walk, make her lie down on the bed and spread her legs apart; then apply the massage technique I have described; and if she doesn't give birth, make her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; and pull out the baby according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to pray as long as the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the baby's exit through its neck, and let her spread her hands, and her buttocks turned towards her mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that you guide their hand, then turn it slowly and gradually, and press lightly; when it's even, place it on the muscle-stretching nature of altitude and oil as we have said, then command her to move slowly; and when you have done this, make her sit down, and command her to pray; and make her snort.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for the rest of the second part.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it proceeds in this manner through the whole second stage, if she completes the second stage up to her nail, until the moisture is discharged; and if the baby can move on its face and neck, then she should cut at her belly, without letting it be held back, and let the baby die; then push the child inside, as long as you have placed him accordingly, and command the woman not to pray once: then gently apply force.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the delivery of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that fleas are born many times, and every time three or four; and this is not unusual, nor does it happen often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are removed and do not live anymore if you don't know them; I know this, that they multiply, and are devoured by the syphilitic humors which affect them, those being bound to the body; and no single time emerge naturally like all others under, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge painfully, as we have said in treatment, and the wound is subtle, then do it quickly and lightly as she does; and do so according to what will promote health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	None of them are formed in Maris I through XV or beyond, they are all formed into the shape of an infant by the measurement of their glory, and it is necessary that the child know all this, because something similar might happen to him; do so according to what is proper.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you are treating the woman who has had an abortion or miscarriage, as I have explained in division, and if it doesn't come out, and you're forced to do manual work; you need to know whether the woman is healthy, and hasn't experienced symptoms of death, or she feels fear for death; you need to ensure that the woman is comfortable on her back, and has her shoulders slightly inclined downwards, and her legs lifted; then guide the woman's neck halfway up, or if bound to the bed so it doesn't hinder the extraction; then rub her lips with moist oil using musk and fennel seeds and linseed; then anoint her hands with these oils and musk substances; then place them gently on her stomach; then let I know where she places the scissors that are suitable for this, and be careful that the child is dressed so it descends onto its head; if you insert the scissors into her abdomen or throat or mouth or tongue or under the beard or collarbone or near the ribs, and if it descends to the feet, place a knife and in the middle of her back; and it should cut the scissors with his right hand, and put the curve between his left fingers, and anoint them gently with all his hands, and insert the scissors into none of these places we have mentioned until he reaches the empty space; this is the form of the scissors:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then strike with another hot iron or the third one if you need it, so that all extractions are equal; and then move equally on both sides, to allow for a smooth extraction, and ensure that the coal is sharp enough to hold during the extraction, as shown here.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part, if the boil touches some of his fingers from which pus oozes, and keep it in that part, and squeeze out the other part; and if no part remains, then place this coal or higher up on him, and do it until all is squeezed out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be returned due to squeezing, you should wrap it around this cloth until everything has come out; then cut in the joint of the sole or at the ankle, and do the same with the other hand. With both feet, do as follows:
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's head is large and it is stuck at the exit, or if its sharp part has assembled together, then you should push in the spiny appendix between your fingers, and make its head assemble and remove the sharp; or you will have it done with the tool called "almidach", which comes with the instruments of the chapter after this one; and so do the same to all the children until there is a large natural opening. And then pull on the bones with tongs, and if the child's head jumps out forcefully and is restrained by force, as long as moisture exists inside it; and if she can't come out, you should cut piece by piece what you can; and if it is inflamed in the abdomen or near the ribs, then you must pierce until the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the fetus is on its feet, there is a slight attraction, and the movement to the mouth of the birth canal is also slight.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stuck in the belly or breast, you should remove it at the folded skin wrap on the hand; and stretch the belly or breast until the moisture that's inside is gone. And if another member is osteitis and the head stays, then press the palm of your hand flat to the maris, and guide it to the mouth of the maris; then you press in from inch one or two, and pull with strength; and if the mouth of the maris is narrowed due to pus that came inside, it's not good to fight over it, instead you should apply moist substances. And administer things like plasters, soak them in water softening agents and moisturizers.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on its side and you can make it even, then apply what we have said about live birth infants; and if there's no possibility, then pull it out piece by piece, making sure not to leave anything of the secondary stage.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, guide the patient to where we have instructed regarding abscesses; and if bleeding occurs during removal, then cool water should be applied restraining it, and other treatments should be administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had given birth to one child in her belly, then another followed from that womb, and this other one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came out in the belly, and it swelled so much that when it opened, it started to cause severe pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for treatment, and I thought for a long time, and couldn't provide proper care for the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed a strong plaster on it, and out came a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, for the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I treated the wound, and guided my hands along the bones, until the woman was in the best position; and I kept the woman lying in this manner for a long time like so, and it would be just a little while after she began to bleed from her nose; and I remember this chapter being only about what to do when, should one of the masters find an unusual thing, they know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring back the wife to her place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the presser, with which books are written; and in each two parts there are four heads of four limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Otherwise, the horns should be more subtle than a restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth should be as wide as half the thickness of the pole, and the edge of the tree should be one and a half palms long; and between these two poles there should be two joints made of the same pole, which are firmly attached on both sides, about half a palm from each other or slightly more; and these two joints are fastened in the mouth of the pole to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another type, more subtle and lighter in appearance, could be made from a stick of ebony or boxwood according to the resemblance of pincers; and it has two heads for two attachments, as you see, each one measuring a palm's length, and two widths wide. And when you observe the uterus open all over the instrument, make the woman lie down at the bed with her legs hanging and her thighs spread out, then hold the two attachments together firmly in the uterus, keeping the top of the instrument between her buttocks; then work your hand around the whole instrument as equally on pincers, according to how you observe the opening size of the uterus mouth, until the fetus does what she wishes.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit. Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bleeding from the root or base, or an abscess, even if the pus is as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle pus within which the skin is constrained:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have discussed the treatment of wounds in the previous section; now we will discuss treatments for hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and depending on where the wounds are located, and for what reason they were caused.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause injuries are due to the action of stones, the size of swords and knives or spears, arrows or sticks, or similar objects; or they occur according to the parts of the body, such as wounds in the neck, head, chest, abdomen, liver, and other bodily limbs. I will tell you how to treat each wound, starting with simple injuries on the head since that topic will be covered in its respective chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or affects the head and there is no fracture of bone, be vigilant about whether it's due to stone or similar conditions. The skin remains often broken across wounds which are large, causing you slight doubt over pus formation. If there is slight bleeding from the wound soon after it occurred, treat the head immediately with salve; if done this way it will heal normally against the necrotic part; and encourage the patient's body to be full of wine and heavy food afterwards.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if they do not want to be treated with salve, if their meat should be reduced, and not drink wine or eat meat; and place it in the wound, if pus has come out, wet cotton with roset oil only, or with astringent wine; and if there is no pus present, place it on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and is not moving due to air, powder that I will mention later; and if it has been burnt by the air, place some remedies over it until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like from a sword cut or similar injuries, and the lips cannot be sewn together with sutures, then they are sewn together, like I will explain in injuries to the abdomen, by sewing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes the bone, it might be able to hold for just a bit if you force it; then treat the wound with medicine, replace hard tissue instead of skin, and instruct the patient on eating large meats, such as testicles and cooked wheat or other similar items.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or come across skin rot, and it doesn't reach the bone, then cut out the rotten part entirely, and bleed it; then treat; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which can't be stopped by medicines, then tie up the artery, and if you find that it has dislocated, tie it with a string; and if this doesn't help, then cauterize.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should apply this powder which binds in such a way that once it's applied, the wound heals.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method for the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; living charcoal three parts, and finely ground it into a powder. Spread this powder evenly over the wound until it well aerates and joins with all its blood; then tie it tightly in place, ensuring not to allow it to swell if it does; for you do not remove the medicine until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And you should not do this with charcoal alone, when you don't have the incense or the dragon's blood, but only that the doctor has cleansed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the heart has made the wound move in its state, indeed in this condition, so do not apply this powder to it; but apply some digestible ointments instead, or oats flour mixed with water and honey, until it stops bleeding; then proceed with other treatments until it heals.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief. de la plaie dou col	from the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound comes from the neck and if it is simple, there should be no difference between it and those in the head, but if a vein or an artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it's the nerves, there is no other tool but to leave the treatment, and not put anything restricting, for it harms the nerves and causes them to recede; do not put anything cold on the wound because the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuity is with the brain which is the highest member; but apply a mild medicine instead, such as water lilies washed in gentle water, mixed with rose oil, and cucumbers washed similarly in gentle water, and other earthy substances according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so it binds in layers, then treat until it heals properly.

And if the wounds are deep and infected with pus, penetrate them or even below them. de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	From the wound of a spear or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a lance or knife wound and the injury goes deep into flesh, observe if there is wind escaping from the wound: know that the wound is fatal. If it doesn't go deep, but is fresh with all its blood, don't put powder on in the first hour, nor tie it for fear of the blood not draining properly to flow outwards and return to heart, and worry the patient; instead apply an attractive ointment, and tie twice a day. If you don't have ointment, place old cotton in the wound to suck out moisture and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days or more; if no spasms or heart tremors occur, it is clear that the patient will recover, provided there are good signs, that you know the injury has been saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit. Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it's simple, or worse, or on the back, treat the one ahead. dou derrompement dou ventre	regarding the protrusion of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The abdominal cuts are large, medium and small; from a major wound any of the intestines or the lining of the intestines might fall out, through which foreign objects can enter. Sewing is more troublesome and in no case is worse than minor wounds compared to major ones because when we reinsert the intestines properly, if they weren't already done so piece by piece; as intestines swell from heat exposure, if reinserted not deeply enough. And thus smaller wounds are better as with abdominal cuts you can easily recover, and I will describe each way of how it happens: there are four main types of cuts affecting the abdomen; common stitches happen in the abdominal cut, and stitches for other body parts follow similar patterns to those injuries; yet all are more fitting in the case of abdominal cuts and I'll explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and no part of the intestine has been damaged or torn, and when a broken bone must be set back into place, this can be done using one of two methods: either because of the size of the wound as we have described, or due to the fact that the intestine becomes swollen from cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm him in this manner: wet a sponge or a slice of meat with water alone, or cook it in boiling water mixed with vinegar and cypress needles, until the intestine becomes so swollen that you can drain it. And once done with these warming procedures, let it cool down to relieve the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, rinse or wash the intestine with water or salted water, for through this method, the entrance allows very little passage; and if it doesn't allow entry, make a small incision at the tool's edge used to remove stitches; and the first treatment is to ensure that the cut is made only when there is great necessity, and not just so; these are the tools to cut into it: you should cut inside in the curve and outward not, and here is how it looks:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound has been enlarged, and the intestines have escaped, if you can place them again according to their natural form in their proper location, then do so because this is beneficial.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is extensive, and it's located on the lower part of the abdomen, you should have the patient lie on their back with their legs higher than their head; and if it's located in the abdominal area, place their head and buttocks higher than the parts below; also, when the rupture occurs in one of the two halves of the belly, you should position yourself so that the side being drained is higher than the other; and thus follow my advice on how to manage such large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have available. Then prepare the surgical knife, which severs the entire wound with its blade and brings together the edges; this is a common method of suturing. You should thread your needle or needles according to the width of the wound; leave about an inch from the edge of the wound before starting, then sew in place by inserting the needle through that part where you will begin. Sew in two parallel strands on each side, then bring together the two edges of the wound slightly, and again leave about an inch before sewing another stitch. Continue sewing as if it were your first stitch until the entire wound is secured; use needles that are neither too thin nor too thick; very fine needles cut all the flesh, but too large ones may not fit well: so they should be medium-sized. Do not place the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, lest they pierce and widen the wound during suturing; after sewing, trim the ends of the needles to prevent them from irritating the patient while sleeping. Cover the needle holes with bandages or cloths for proper healing support until the wound has healed completely. This method of stitching is more suitable for small wounds because you would use one thread or two for a second stitch, which is common, and involves bringing together the skin edges and intestine edges onto one needle where there's strong medium thread; after piercing these four in sequence, pull out the needle from where you started like sewing through cloth. Leave about an inch between each stitch equivalent to one finger width; this suture heals a person, and I have stitched a wound that was made by a knife on the abdomen, which had been cut with a sword and was several inches wide, containing intestines as long as two palms of length, and it had a wound in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestines until it had been 24 hours since he had them, and the wound was sewn up until 15 days, and I treated him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the surgeon had judged that he was going to die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in the middle of a region where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put old cotton twice on the wound each day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of suturing: take the needle and insert it from outside to inside at the beginning; when it has pierced the heart straight in straight, place the tip of your finger or guide where the needle has been inserted, and make it pierce again from inside to outside at another point; and the principle of this suture is that you stitch just like the squirrel furs themselves, leaving a loop on one side and then taking it up again on the other, until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen correctly states, is like what others do, who join the two parts together naturally. They apply one end of silk thread to the other end and sew in such manner: insert a needle or thread close to the middle of each, then make only one incision on this side, leaving both ends of the silk thread; after that, turn the needle, making it pierce from below up until beneath, passing by both ends of the silk thread. Then make two more punctures through from underneath down to inside beneath both ends, using two other pieces of thread that are the opposite sides' ends. And this is how stitching is done and most commonly performed.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen spoke these words and no one denies it. One should stitch the belly with two needles or threads each having a piece of thread at both ends. The stitches must be placed on opposite sides in the manner of those who sew in a crosswise pattern; now know this, that when the injury is within the belly, the stitching there is more painful than elsewhere in their abdominal region.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as with other wounds: and it's that when you find the fresh wound filled with all its blood, just like when the surgeon has treated it, then sew up the intestines, and the cut; then apply a spreading powder on the flesh. And if the surgeon has treated it, apply no ointment until the wound heals; and check the stitches, and ensure they are sealed properly for intestinal leakage and abscesses; then treat the wound as with others until healed; and if you have no medicine, immediately upon its starting to heal, use old cotton, and move it twice a day till healed.
