Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it has often affected cattle, and it's a small worm that comes forth between skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body going up and down, causing pain at each part of the body until it reaches the skin where it goes, then bursts; and it's accompanied by gangrene from various fluids, such as coming towards worms and maggots and roundworms or in the stomach; doubt is cast on its severity, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes near the eye, by chance it enters, destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and cured, know that one must wait until: then you should bind the arm up and down with a strong tight bandage, then cut upwards and treat it there; and if the wound is deep in the flesh, and you can't find it, then burn it with fire while it bleeds; and whatever major injuries are done are when the wound contacts your eye, as we have mentioned; and if you see it coming or getting close to the eye, then hold over him firmly that part of the eye and cut upwards; and you should use the remedy of purification of body substances through medicines in solution for the putrid humors, and avoid eating spoiled meat that might cause corruption.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it's a pain that affects some body parts, and then moves from part to part; I have seen the case as I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to attend a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of her arm; shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm was climbing up to her shoulder, faster than anything else, like molten silver when cut from one thing to another; the pain left that particular area, and settled into the shoulder, then gradually spread throughout the body until it reached the other arm; then she told me that the pain continued inside her body, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was marveling much how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	In this way, I have wished for many things to cause pain from one part of the body to another, but I had not experienced it myself until I saw it in the woman; and I thought that was due to her having a dry body, with exposed veins, and because of which appeared this constrainted wind-like sensation; and they do not seem to appear according to this reason in those who are healthy, and have moist bodies and retracted veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we said, you should press it down and around quickly; and then keep pressing until the wind force escaping from its place comes out; and cauterize the place. And if you do not observe it at your eyes, you must treat the one who releases the wind force, such as with stinky pills, serapin pill, and other similar things.
des saiettes	Des saiettes" in this context likely refers to "extracting arrows". In medieval medical practices, physicians would often deal with wounds caused by arrows or projectiles, requiring them to be removed from the body.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, depending on their appearance and according to the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their sizes is such that there are those with large points, small ones, hooked ones and soldered ones; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those which have pieces; and the one who expels in no member, it does so according to two ways: or in a primary limb, like the head, heart, liver, lungs, intestines, bladder, and other major limbs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she gives birth then in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: it is necessary that you prepare for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various conditions; and when this bad sign does not appear and the arrow has not been fully removed, then draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow penetrates and pierces the bone, and jumps the fluid that is above the brain, it's when blindness, stiffness, inversion, redness in the eyes, and feverishness and tongue inflammation, and muscle spasms and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes lacks strength from the nose or ears; and sometimes loss of speech and voice; and a white moist wound discharge resembling pus, and also burns like ashes; and if this sign appears, prepare for treatment, and pull out the arrow if it hasn't.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it is in or through the heart, indicates that it's near the left breast. It also feels as if something hard was stuck inside rather than empty; and sometimes the arrow stops moving like a pulse, and causes black blood to come out, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore know without doubt that many will die from this injury.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that never leaves its path is when blood spurts from the wound without foam, and the throat swells up, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly while their body grows cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow stops inside the leg's fur, it is located below the small ribs; and there is great bleeding and great pain and sighing; and all limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach penetrates it, perchance something of the undigested meat comes from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach pierces it, and if there is no meat in the intestines after jumping from the wound, then there's no hope for treatment, nor extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow penetrates into the bladder, and urine flows out and escapes after jumping from the wound, and patients feel intense pain: know that this injury is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts, such as the limbs (including arms and legs), neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, back, spine, knees, and feet, as well as any similar parts, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the nerve or artery and it isn't venomous, as I will tell you that this happened to me, because what you did was different.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one of the men that an arrow hit him in the shoulder at the base of his nose: I tried it out and pulled it away from the other side through the fat of the ear, causing no particular discomfort.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	I pulled out an arrow that hit him in the fat around his eye near the paper underneath, and the arrow was recovered. Only its tip reached towards the shaft, and the arrow was about the size of a Turkish bow, all made of iron without feathers; the game hunter felt no harm after it and there were no bad incidents.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arab ear arrow: I would let the stubble grow, and sharpened as much as possible while pulling it, and healed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pulled an arrow out of the house, which was stuck in his back or belly, and thought he would die; and then after thirty days had passed, if it didn't change its position; I cut near the arrow, removed it, and pulled it out, without any bad incident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you observe a house where an arrow has fallen on the back or down, and the wound is healed up; and stays inside him, without changing its natural positions, and doesn't find any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And look at another man, who was struck in the face with an arrow and had stitches put into his wound; and he endured suffering from great pain afterwards; and many others are similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And there was an arrow shot at the king's court in the home of princes, where it was stuck between his nose and chin, and was slightly tilted to the right side; and the arrow was fully lodged. I was summoned for treatment after three days when it was shot.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried to treat it with all my skill and did not feel anything; and there was a pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow. I put a adhesive and digestive plaster on his ear, because the ears were not inflamed; and then appeared the arrow's ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the plaster to his hands for days, and quickly healed the wound. Then he stayed thus long with the patient, until he felt the arrow inside his nose on the third day; and that's what I told him.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive aqua regia medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened and then tried it. I felt the tip of the arrow as it moved towards his head; afterward, I adjusted in the wound opening using this same corrosive medicine until I clearly saw the tip of the arrow; and I passed through very well all inner parts for about four months, and then finished closing the wound so tightly that when I tried to open it again from both sides, I couldn't. Then I kept refining and engineering ways to create instruments, until on one day, using well-made forceps as shown towards the end of this chapter, I could manipulate it and leave the wound closed after applying them; throughout this process, I was very careful to avoid harming him in any way.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeons judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will then restore it, and if the wound is sealed, and made whole for the patient completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you about the quality of extracting some arrows, so place your treatment on what I do not mention, because books cannot grasp everything; but the wise masters compare well to a few large things, and to that which is present and lacking, they find new works, and new tools, in the removal of things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows penetrate the limbs where they are driven in through two ways: either by their natural side or through another part; and the one that pierces through or enters it is an arrow entering its flesh, and now never again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let her stay until the flesh inside is rotten and cleansed; and when this has happened, let her out. And also if she's stuck in the bone and can't come out, leave her like that for some days and remove a little each day; then she will jump. If she doesn't jump, penetrate deep into all her secret parts until the inner flesh becomes wider, and then guide her.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, extending to one of the organs of the brain, and all the events that I have mentioned happen openly to the patient: do not remove her immediately, but let her stay until she becomes level after some days, because if the arrow reaches so far, it's death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not reach so far, yet remains within the patient for several days without any bad incident, then use the device to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it's so deeply stuck and cannot come out at all, then use internal threads such as I have instructed you; then treat the wound until it is clean.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow has been returned inside your body and you cannot see it, seek it with all your effort; and if you feel it, try to pull it out without any suitable instrument. And if the wound is too tight or the arrow is deep within and there are no bones, nerves, or veins, remove the arrow as much as possible when the wound is large; and then pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold onto the arrow at its base, extract the flesh that sticks out from two parts of your body until it moves under your touch, and then break or bend the arrow's ears, as long as you can pull it out. And be careful not to break the arrow when pulling it, ensuring you pull it more tightly instead.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it in one go, leave it until its entire length is rotted away by maggots, then try to pull it out, as extraction requires effort.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you do otherwise, then follow what we have said about treatment in our chapter; and beware of incising near nerves and veins, and apply as much pressure as possible to pull out the arrow without risk, fast or slow, hard or gently; and place the patient according to how they were when the arrow fell upon them, because this provides the greatest help, and if you cannot, then place them according to what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or where there is no opening in it, or the skin is swollen at that place so one can see or feel something: then cut upwards, as long as you can grasp with your tongs, and then squeeze: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is held in the bone, twist your hand round as long as she enters the bone and widens the bone, then pull her out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it in for now and then continue the extraction as long as it comes out; and if there is an arrow part left, keep pulling until you pull out everything; and if it's just a bullet, when you apply pressure to administer force, if you apply tool pressure, so that the arrow point goes into the tool hair; and then push forcefully, and if the arrow is stuck in the hair of the tool, push the tool with its point entering first to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is encased, it must be that you remove all the flesh around or where I am entering, if possible, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow is in the leg or arm or abdomen or bladder or rib area, and it's close to vital organs, you can cover up, if possible; but avoid covering over a vein and nerve. Then remove the arrow, and then treat the wound while it heals; and treat until it is healed completely.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used for arrows is similar to the tip of a bird's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead resembles the feathers of a bird, because it tapers to the tip of the arrow, as this is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers for pushing and pulling as such is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the horns of common veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	The veins from which one can bleed are thirty-one, from which sixteen have their origin. That is: two batans located behind the ears, which are called "two grasses"; and the two arteries found in the two visible temples; and two veins that run through the corners of the eyes, known as "aspires"; and the vein running down the forehead; and the vein around the nose's root; and the two jugulars located at the neck; and the two veins situated above the mouth on the cheeks, which are called "augéherich"; and two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly treated consist in each arm: one is the cephalic vein and it is found on the left side; they call this 'vein of the head'. And the middle one is called 'fistula', made up from cephalic and basilic veins, and they refer to this as 'vein of the heart'. The basilic vein itself may be on either the left or right side, they refer to this as 'vein of the belly', it's located under the clavicle; this is the one that gets treated, whose opening becomes clearly visible in the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The arteriole is the vein located between the little finger and the ring finger, and it is found in two places. In the leg and near the ankle, there are three veins: one of which is underneath the bend of the ankle on the left side of the shin, and the second, known as 'sophene', is at the ankle on the right side of the shin; and the vein referred to as 'ness' that is in the other ankle. In the other leg are three veins below those.[clarification needed]
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The treatment of vein diseases located behind the ears helps with cataracts and migraines. de la sainie des leivres	Of surgical treatment of wounds
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The care of veins in the mouth aids in collection within the mouth, and contributes to gum decay, and splits in lips, and nosebleeds and internal bleeding.

et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it's more refined and pointed, used to heal fine veins, or one with fine yellow blood.

The treatment of the basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are in the throat, and around the neck, and inside the chest, and in the abdomen; and it's important for the surgeon to treat it carefully, and to be aware of the artery that is nearby.

And if you see it protruding as high as a child's urine, and the semen is red and subtle, know that this is from the artery: hurry then, place your finger for a long time, then remove your finger when it stops bleeding, which has happened many times; grasp the arm, and leave him like that, do not move the body; and proceed in fear, and do not move until he becomes sane.

La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bathing is that bathing should only be done to maintain health and to avoid future diseases. The treatment for diseases does not have a set time limit, but rather must be provided whenever the need arises, day or night, at all times; and it is not appropriate to treat children up to twelve years old, nor pregnant women beyond one quarter of their pregnancy until seven months.

Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses. Therefore, you should not apply anything from what we have discussed here, for fear of harming the artery; but have it properly plastered dry to harden the area, then proceed with another treatment until it heals.

des sainies de ventouse	of suction healings
