Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup used heated like this is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it should have two lengths of half a palm each way across the front, and be placed in the middle at an inch thick from the side, as if to push a needle through, like one might use a needle or an awl, ensuring not to prick the patient when placing on the limb; and it has one middle part that crosses diagonally of the length of an arched arrow or iron for setting up a lamp to be placed both in large applications and small depending on the disease and age of those taking them; because suction cups on children are different than those of adults, and those who are thin differ from those who are fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus should we place this suction cup onto the limb: take a candle or thread of wax and insert it through the middle of the metal rod within the suction cup, ensuring that light is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it doesn't burn the patient; then put it on the limb, set your thumbs where I said earlier, so when you want to do this, if moisture goes in from under it and you remove the suction cup; and use the wax thread as before, and repeat often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction method therefore which is administered in pleurisy disease, at all its stages, there should be neither a fever nor loss of strength, and it is only applied forcefully when it is full of water, and placed solely on the body; this is how it should be done:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Blades are only used when limbs cannot be treated with suction due to their small size, as for lips and gums, and similar parts; and in the absence of disease spots on these areas, such as joints or nails, and others like them; and concerning the quality of usage, it is that if you find blades that are in gentle water without discomfort when used, use them; and place them in gentle water until they become accustomed, with nothing inside their stomachs; then clean with suction and blade, then rub the limb so that it turns red, and place on the blades; and once they're full and shedding, if there's a spot where you can put a suction cup, put it there because this is very effective afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this doesn't work, lift the arm with hot and then cold water, in moderation, and proceed by rubbing. If the limb is too sore after the removal of veins, moisten a linen cloth with cold water and place it on until the veins are healed; if there are many veins, apply powdered vitriol or gall and similar substances until they heal. Or you should place half-cooked peeled peas under the arm, leave them until they evaporate in the arm, which will now stop bleeding. And if you need more, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the veins don't take again, rub the arm with fresh blood, or you should stick an awl into it until blood flows out, and then place it. And when they start to smell the blood, which evaporate; and as soon as you see them bleeding, sprinkle a little aloes powder and finely ground cumin, or ashes, and they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and restoring and resetting of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people in this chapter look at its contents, which they have never seen in any old books or read from letters; and because of this reason, this knowledge has been taken away from our land, for I could not find anyone who had it good; and I know nothing about it, having learned through the knowledge of ancient books that I studied extensively to the point of treating its science, as well as through experimentation and with my lifetime's experience. And in this chapter, I have described what is contained here, summarized it at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the instruments used, just like I did in the previous two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we outline or provide an introduction to this book containing the essence of knowledge and the chapters where the wise person applies their understanding, staying true to reality. So that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a break or dislocation or twists, or any other ailment affecting the joints, it's important to quickly cleanse the injured person on both sides of the body and in between; if there's nothing urgent, such as frailty due to old age, youthfulness, or weakness; if the limb is too stiff or too cold; or if you find hard and frozen joints like ice jousts, or eye and goat flesh. Don't drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and don't fill your stomach with foods that could make your veins too full of blood until you're sure there's no pus in the abscess, or any spreading of matter in the limb; if this condition improves after a day under your initial care.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you feed the patient with meats that cause significant nourishment, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and chestnuts, and pies, and veal spleen, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For such nourishment leads to movement and more quickly heals the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones of old and weak people cannot be well repaired or joined according to their nature due to the drying out of limbs, nor those also who are too tender, such as the bones of young children; but in any case, set the broken bone together with its large tendons and join the limb back into place until it is strong enough again just as before; do not finish your work prematurely, and for this reason you should nourish yourself with large meaty cuts, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breaks come in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a break at the neck is different from a break at the knee or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks leading to war, and others through preparation, as with the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And in cases of injury along with breaks, and breaks resulting from a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its own instrument and proper tool in the restoration, according to what memory brings to his mind; and is known that bone breaking occurs when the limb is twisted and opens well from underneath, and feels pressed by hand pressure; and when there is no twist or movement at the joint, and the patient does not feel much pain, if there's no breakage; but it can have a twist, or crack, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the remedies that come next, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breaking which went in battle and had its two parts disjointed, they must now put them to equal length so that the pus bag can be placed between them; if pus bags come out, leave none of it for as long as the pus is calm. Then make them equal at the point where you can gently and wisely move them, knowing that the restoration in this case is easier than in those with pieces missing; then hold it firmly, just as detailed after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bones have broken pieces and are divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet or a small limb on your hand, or at two strings, or one string and in your hand; place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are reduced, you pull them by all means towards their ends as far as possible, and be careful not to cause injury or pain with your work; adjust the two ends of the bones well according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it's not quite right: if you treat it beautifully, and don't strain it too much, don't press it as those who bring it about by their method of pus evacuation and muscle contraction do to the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limbs are in place, be very careful with the patient so they don't move them, neither while awake nor asleep, neither on turning or in any other way; and ensure well that the limbs are secured enough to not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they do not feel any pain, it is not properly set, and you should put them in such a position that they do not feel any pain; and guard that they are placed correctly, so that no twisting appears when they are restored; and the quality of the broken limb must match what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that limbs broken are diverse in smallness and largeness, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs such as arms and legs, and those similar: it is necessary to wrap them in soft, fine linen. For larger limbs like thighs and calves: it is necessary to wrap them with a broad and firm band, because wide bands embrace the entire limb and constrain it evenly from all sides, so that no twist appears when they are restored; then tie lightly around joints, three or four times according to the limb, and hold your hand on each band a little, then move upwards from the breakage point and constrain less, allowing the breakage to go back slightly; and soften the band gradually until you touch the healthy part of the limb significantly. Then take another band again, twist around it closely on the broken limb; then return below the breakage area and apply moderate pressure, neither too strong nor too weak, as we have described in our previous instruction; then place linen or cloth bands between the twisted linens until they are all even, then tie everything up with a belt, and then place your well-made pins on top, if there is no pus or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something soothing for the abscess against it and which relieves the swelling. Then leave in that state for a few days; after that apply to your stars, and be of half the length of one inch long, or from the shaft used for quills, or from palm leaves, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the stars that one puts on the break be a bit larger and wider than the others; and be as long as they are suitable for limbs of smallness or greatness; then apply them to your stars in the same way you did with the first application, then tie an additional thread above them like at the first application on the break; make it tighter here, less there; and should that thread be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft linen. For if the thread is thick, as in works that fasten strings using their linet tortoise's string making procedures, this is a great mistake because the application cannot be uniform if it is too slender, and it does not suit having less than half a space between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the muscles are stretched by the bones after constriction in their joints, put over them bandages of linen or coarse wool, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When a wound is bleeding and the joints are broken, I will provide the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to strictly bind all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it may not be suitable to apply these splints for seven or eight days after, depending on the healing of any abscesses that occur; and here is how the old plastering method was used to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists: you take flour which is kept at the mill walls, mix it with plenty of egg, make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick, then use it. This is the common method of restoring fractures in multiple ways, and equally for women and children, as it isn't overly hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way to apply plaster that restores fractures and dislocations: take 3 parts of barley, dahlia, rue, and asafetida, and add gum Arabic and mint, with a total of .x.З.; myrrh and aloes, totaling .v.З.; garlic, in the amount of .viiij. З.; grind these ingredients to make a powder, then mix it thoroughly with eggs; if the consistency of this plaster is warm, use it for treatment, as it has a good composition, quickly sets broken bones right, and is effective on many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another plastering method for twists: take mugwort and valerian, each in 1/3 part; myrrh and aloes, each in 9 parts; caragana in 6 parts; Armenian balm in 10 parts. Grind them well, then mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plastering joints and bones in their place, alleviating the arising pain, and using bone saws and lacerations: take new wool, and cook it with fat and oil, then apply this on top of them.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Wound plastering does not heal completely but it is better for soothing abscesses and properly mending bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of dressing broken bones for healing: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial elm leaves, grind them together, then apply as a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the repair of bone fractures and to alleviate the pain caused by the wound.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, groundnuts, each one part; grind them and mix with wine, then apply to warm limbs. If the limbs are hot, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use this application.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of plastering more forcibly than the first, when hard pus comes to the healing of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalve, and sesame seed, balmroot, melilot, and sansucius, and flowers of violet and chamomile, all in one part; grind and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the warmth of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras in his book states that only balm made of beeswax and oil should be applied to the broken limb for restoration purposes, and nothing else. He also indicates it should be between two substances that are neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems like Galen suggests we should apply something to the broken limb for restoration; some things that are dry but a bit warm, such as mirr (myrrh), aloes, and incense, and similar substances, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take maguey (agave) and wool from human corpses, or bird feathers, and mustard leaves, and equal parts of these, grind them, and make a plaster with them and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then take it lightly a little later, and watch that the patient doesn't feel any pain, nor is he moving his bone at its place; if you don't remove it by hand, and if pain comes to the limb or itching, without rest or swelling, should you hurry, and remove it with haste, putting on plaster now; take a light wrap, and a wet sponge from the sea, dip it in water, and immerse the limb until the itching stops and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then place on dry hay moistened in water or oil, bind it with a mat, until you are sure of having removed all pus; and cool down any inflammation in the limb, and remove the pain, then start the subtle repositioning again, with just a little plaster, don't pull too hard as before; and apply it delicately until he is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus and redness, pain, swelling are still present everywhere in the area, indicating inflammation, then you need to apply plaster and bandage again, so start doing this as you did before, equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if no part comes back from what we have said, or the release must be delayed until after three days, four days, five days, or seven; and leave it alone for twenty days according to our observation, as long as there is a breaking sensation, and adjusting the flesh upwards towards the bone; then you must restrain more than initially and increase his meat supply, just as I said before. And if you see that his skin dries too much, know that no resumption can occur; pour cold water over it every time you release him, and do this on each third day, and clean a little at the wound; by this act, cut off the resumptions from the limb, and hasten the healing process against what the ignorant menders are doing, who permanently distort the limb: that's bad news, and these are poor practices. I see nothing else but to let it rest and operate properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes occur. The causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the neck breaks all the bone up to the syfac which is under the bone, just like what is done with hammers or spears. For this reason, such a method of fracture is called "hitting" or "bludgeoning".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword crushes the bone from above without piercing it, this method of fracture is called 'absolute' fracture; and both large and small wounds result from these two types of fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or a crack or neck of stone, or through stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break at the bone, which comes up to the membrane beneath the bone, or above it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound affects bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, thus it's called this kind of fracture "hairline"; and if the injury occurs through hitting with rock or falling or similar actions causing part of the bone to enter the body cavity as if blacksmiths hammer into pots; then the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This often happens in those with soft bones like children's heads; and occurs through all these methods of fracture where small fragments are released, like arrows; and I will speak about it in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all ways of breaking through extraction from them, and investigation with attempts, and through the corrupted matter which is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs it together, then the dark fracture opens.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be vigilant about maladies and if you see no adverse event such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, stretching, swelling, fever ague, and if the eyes emit and turn red or other similar symptoms in various conditions, it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming occurrence, yet still hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the nose comes to you first, and it's in winter, it is fitting to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month you could.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the pus under the bone becomes infected, and the accidents we have said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the breakage of bone reaches up to the membrane that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut off the broken section in this way: and take the head of the patient's flesh to expose on the bone in all possible ways, and on the appearance of the wound as much as possible. And if blood flow comes out at discovering the bone, or pus appears, use what should be used there, then you fill the empty space with damp cloth in olive oil; and let the wound rest until the pus is calmed and it's sure that there won't be any more bleeding. Then begin to cut through the bone, this is done according to two ways of working: one way is that you make a narrow cut in front, and this is its form.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut of about double the size of the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method involves making various cuts of different sizes, some narrow and others wide, with sharp points, made from iron; and you should do this gently so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is protruding and hard, it is necessary that you puncture through it internally, in such a way that you administer cuts with needles, not entirely so that they do not pierce beyond the bone's edge, and must have above the point a margin or one circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than this, so that each goes into its place of the thickness of the bone, so that you have needles for all its edges; and this is the form of the three ways of using needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the bone internally is that you place one needle on the bone, and twist with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced. Then put the needle elsewhere a little after, and do this all internally. After that, cut out the space between the parts of the bone using the incisors, and do so more finely and gently than possible, as we have said, until you bring the bone to your hand or any tool you have such as forceps, tweezers; and be sure not to touch the brain nor the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is fitting that you rework the preparation that has remained of the bone with any other similar instrument like a scalpel. But it must be more robust and finer than the other scalpel; and if there remains nothing from the small bones or no scales, then gently scrape them off with these tools; and then treat the wound with ointments and remedies as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of treatment is this which Galen stated, who says it is safer; and he pulls very strongly, and that's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to uncover part of the bone, where the break opens and moves, so that once you have uncovered that part, you will place under the tip of this oblong incision, which has this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side alone, and have the part split into two halves, so that you are cutting towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, ensuring you lightly touch the entire bone surface, and be well cautious of any fabric under it. If it feels soft against the bone, tap it gently as you won't cause harm or fear to the bone tissue.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break doesn't go through the membrane, and only part of the bone is cut above, with small pieces remaining, after smoothing that area it is necessary to remove the scales using a fine shaver you must have in various quantities. To apply the most suitable for each place according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	When facing large shavers, then proceed to finer ones, and never cease this practice until it's done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair cutting tasks and subtle breaks, you must adapt according to their direction; and this matter is not resolved for him who has devoted his study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the scab is revealed, you should take linen according to the size of the wound and soak it in a mixture of oil and roset oil, then place it over the wound. Then take another piece of double linen (either twice or thrice layered), soak it in wine and roset oil, and place it on top of the first linen layer; do this more gently than you can, making sure not to weigh down the scab, then apply the second bandage from above, but don't pull it too tightly that it only touches the wound; leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess settles completely. Then remove the bandages and administer medicines such as lily roots, myrrh powder, frankincense powder, and similar things; make a powder from these substances and apply them to the wound, then administer local medicines that don't cause irritation. And be cautious to keep the wound clean, do not leave any ointment on it or let any poultice assemble on it because when poultices come together over the brain tissue, they spread and are harmful to the patient; for if something sharp is put on the scab, it will irritate from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take heed, if no accidents befall the patient as we have said, if it is doubtful, then there should be no fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fear does not come out only because of the medicine we have put on, that virtue exists, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of roset oil and a dratel in glue, and you apply it to your skin; then you treat with treatment methods as they should be done until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two neck bones above, or one by itself, should be broken for this reason; they are two bones. The one below is cartilaginous and does not break, even if you try to bend or twist it, and afterwards it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should pinch your little finger or around your nose tip, and place this break inside your index finger, and out from your nostril, until the nose revives according to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain through your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose, and cannot come to his nose, then it's necessary that you place him level with the head of a rod a bit thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is two parts in size, redo this procedure and try to restore it on the first day if possible; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, once the abscess has subsided, pinch at the nose tip with lin cloth. If the break is located in one part, do so.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another poultice on the other side, if the break is there; and let them be large enough to fill the depressions near the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that when restoring one must smear the stumps with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem right to me but it is necessary that they be moistened in the preparation of a yolk ointment and flour; then leave the stump until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one uses goose feathers instead of tents, and if it is one egg's worth of fat in the middle, and the wound heals, and breaths through the patient; then do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if pus comes out through the nose as you are working, then put moistened lint or cotton in oil mixed with rose water, or a spoonful of almond oil.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses are not coming out, you should apply plaster on top, made of ground myrrh and incense powder mixed with yolk ointment, then place it on thin wafers, without tying them tightly; and if the contents break into small pieces when pricked by the nails, use suitable instruments to remove the pieces, then cut along the incision and clean the wound, joining it back together using plasters and ointments suitable for that purpose; and if there is no infection under the nails, treat the stump, and place cloves on it until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is broken outwards, and there is no wound outwardly visible, only the break is outwardly present, not being split into two parts externally but cracked internally. If one knows this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the breakage occurs in the right part, you press your index finger into the mouth near the wound. And if the breakage is in the left mandible, then press your index finger of your right hand, and gently press the break internally, and perform this action with the other hand outwardly, making sure it's even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jawbone is split into two parts, it should be treated with an extension of both hands until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth occurs, or a rupture, hold them with a thread made of gold, silver or silk. Then place on the broken mandible wax, and place underneath two double cloths; then place on one cloth a large triangle well made, or an equal piece of leather long and wide according to the mandible's size. Tie it in place as much as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and have them eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, release it on the third day and then reposition what has become distorted; apply plaster with some powder from a mill mixed with plenty of egg or saffron flour after removing the wax; place wool under the plaster for warmth, and if the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change, let them remain like that until they heal; many recover in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if it comes to incision at the foot, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is both fracture and wound together, reward is null for any bone fragment that has been removed; such subtlety of extracting requires instruments suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and there remains none, if the wound is wide, place one poultice suitable for this over it to encourage flesh growth until healing occurs.
de la forcele	by the strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks multiple times in front of the shoulder, towards it, and the breaking occurs in three ways: or it is broken and severed in two parts, with pieces present, and it is easier to restore; or there is a break accompanied by injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And for the procedures when the break is due to injury, have two ministers, so that one examines the shoulder where the force has broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part. Then set the break equal with your hands, so that its form be as it should, and let not any appearance or movement be seen.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, place a round sponge of cloth or wool under the shoulder towards the leg; make its size according to your needs. Stretch and lift the broken force, hold the sponge in your hand so that you can set the break equal, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the force to the outside due to it coming forwards, then the patient should lie with their head on their shoulder blade, and place a pillow under one shoulder. de la brisure du bras	"Of the breaking of the arm"
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "foscile" pair. Of these, one is small and it's this one that surrounds the hand; and the other is large, and it's this one that is underneath, in front of the small finger. Sometimes only one of the large fosciles breaks, or sometimes the smaller one does, and occasionally they both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small fracture is broken, it's advisable to gently stretch and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it's the large fracture, you'll need to pull more forcefully. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the eyes evenly, according to their best form.

Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the wounding in an injury, I spoke about it in the singular chapter; then take care of the treatment.

Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And restore the member and the ligament after a few days.

And if any bad accidents happen to the member, such as itching that appears on the member, you should dip the member in hot water as long as that itch is alleviated; and leave the member not to be moved until it rests.

de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand

de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand
