And if you cannot return the bone back, as we have said, if you have an appropriate tool for this purpose, such as a scalpel or a knife, at your power; then cut the one that is stuck in the bone with hardness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it has not been placed in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you want it to be in its place, then apply a moist lint cloth soaked with black and clean vinegar. And if that is the case for an external wound; do not put wax or any other thing ointment on the wound; otherwise it could cause infection and decay; then give these remedies after restoring the bone and leave the wound uncovered, cover the entire body part according to the size of the wound, make sure you take good care so that the wound is not tightened with pressure; many times this was done by foolish people, leading to death or rot in the patient on numerous occasions; and let the compresses be softer and more soothing compared to other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you doubt that there may be injuries there, as we have said, and you find pain in the head, then it does not suit to place remedies on it; but envelop within, instead of remedies, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound has begun to heal, remove what you had placed with all the wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, such as the four-formula ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is united and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it should be that the limbs are placed so that the wound heals in such a way that the bone comes together lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal otherwise than at once with the bone, know that there are small fragments of bone, which is why you should work on the wound with traction, and remove all these unnecessary pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a sinus appears in the head or any other form of infection, it is necessary to treat it according to what he instructs in the chapter mentioned earlier.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed in the body part, like the bone of the hip or shoulder, or other large limbs, do not treat it because many die from it. However, leave it until it heals naturally; perhaps it will heal on its own after twenty days or thirty. Then, if you can, treat the wound; but if you cannot, let it be as it is.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The blows that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come across various effects after the healing of injuries due to the breeze. Indeed, it is something to see how the limb's shape changes; and by chance, cannot perform its natural tasks on the limb.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then in dealing with these things: if they are inflamed due to heat or cold, administer stictic medicines like aloes, frankincense, myrrh, sarsaparilla, senna, and similar others, as you see fit among any of these substances, or all together, and mix them with stictic wine or with plenty of eggs or with garlic; and apply them to the wound in poultices, pressing it well, but not letting it move in your hands during the day; then remove it, and repeat another one until the pus is extracted; or you can apply on a well-made piece of plaster; for the properties of plaster are that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the pus has hardened like stone, so it needs to be removed, then scrape off any excess above it, and leave the treatment as long as it heals.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb that is weak after a siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, it happens for many reasons: due to one factor being that they were tied too tightly, not as they should have been; or because there were too many bands, not allowing normal circulation in the limb; or because of an excess of swelling; or due to too large movements at inappropriate times; or because they have little blood in their body, making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment involves making the patient eat well, and make the body tender until the pulse grows in him; then give them baths, and bring him joy and comfort. Afterwards apply ointment to the limb so that the ointment attracts to the large swelling, and cleanse it with water often, until the swelling corresponds to the limb; and restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If the member is twisted after recovery.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and if the bones are broken apart, while the shape of the body is ugly afterwards, it does not lose its natural function: nor should you believe those who say one must break the limb anew; many people do this in our land; these operations are criticized and cause great harm, even to the point of death. However, if the bruises and injuries are fresh, then they should be treated with hot water or softifying herbs, like leaves from valerian, roots, and thyme, among others; and apply a poultice made from them; you can also take fat figs, grind them with flour from rye, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation. And make an ointment for poultices, as properly done salve, and take valerian root, mix it with grease from lard or oil of safflower, and apply this as a poultice; alternatively, you can take fat figs, grind them with rye flour, and similar remedies that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never let the dislocation occur by rubbing constantly and for long periods with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow some movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like bone, and needs to be removed with the iron, if it suits one must cut up until reaching the bone, with a slight, gentle incision. And apply concentration and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, because it cannot move then, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation affects none, if it suits now to bring back without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the limbs swell, and by chance it might move to points within; because one should not move the limb when it is swollen: many times pus and other pains come about; however, whenever this happens, have a surgeon tend to the patient, then let him rest until the abscesses are calmed; then immerse the member in warm water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes into its own place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat bony at their roots and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and expel saliva from the mouth so that one cannot hold it, nor close their mouth, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And when it is whole and completed, you should reset it quickly without hesitation; and do this in such a manner that the helpers cut the head of the patient, and place his earlobes under the socket of the dislocated jawbone inside the mouth, if the dislocation is bilateral; and each hand should be outside, to make them equal. And instruct the patient to soften, his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And hold the thumbs in place until they settle back into position.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if bringing them back causes pain, especially when the two jaws are together, so that the heads of bones from hot water and oil, as long as they are gently brought back; do not overly force it to bring back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the sick person closes well after being mollified, then place wet cloths in a poultice made from rosin-oil and beeswax, then loosely bind them with moist thread; and let the sick person rest on their back, and their limbs should be between two cushions, so they don't move to either side, nor try to stretch at all, but only eat light food until the pains are gone and the jaw is closed; and then let him taste lightly afterwards, and doesn't struggle to open his mouth when eating or drinking, until the jaw is well healed and restored.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be placed in their proper position within an hour, and are not returned to them, it leads to fevers that become habitual, and at times abdominal pain, and at times vomiting of clear contents.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is loss; and many times, death has befallen those to whom it happens, within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the forceful (context unclear without more information)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot relieve the pain from within the body's continuity or from its backside; it can only be relieved once outside, and this is clearly felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And for the restoration process, let them lie on their back and extend their arms. Then shape it like a hand in your palm, and they will return to this position; then place it with the plaster bandage and apply pressure, then strain it. If the foot does not dislocate again, leave it alone; but if it does happen once, reset it to its original location as we have described; then place it with the plaster and bandage, strain it, and instruct the sick person to rest until they are healed; thus in this way is returned the dislocation of the shoulder blade when it has been taken out of its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is only dislocated in three ways: from which one way it dislocates towards the elbow part and away from underarm; and the second way it dislocates at the bottom of the foot; and by chance dislocates at the top part, and this happens rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder or inside through nerves; and many times dislocates downwards towards the elbow even for those who have little muscle tissue because in these cases she dislocates quickly; for those who have enough muscle tissue it jumps to points and comes back to points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men through impact or bruising, and swells the shoulder with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must verify it as long as you are certain; then you may begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And know about the shoulder dislocations when it moves downward towards the elbow, and you will notice differences between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find various obvious diversity among them; and you will discover a hollow at the head of the shoulder, and from the elbow to the shoulder, just like if it was an eye. And the patient cannot bring her hand to her nose with the diseased shoulder or move in any way; and similarly, if she is dislocated upwards, it isn't hidden either, because you can find it clearly at the collarbone; and this type of dislocation doesn't allow bringing back when it's new, or if its child is diseased.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the ministers lift their hand from the flesh at the top, then place their palms under the armpit, and raise the joint up to its full height by force; and the ministers lift their hand and extend it up high, placing it underneath; if it comes too quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it doesn't come out as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water. And the attendant should apply a soothing and relieving treatment to them; for example, decoction of garlic, fenugreek, and milk thistle in water, which should be administered internally; after that, the patient should rest with their back immersed. Place a cloth of equal texture, neither too soft nor too hard, under their back, then place a stool underneath them, and have someone hold onto the heel of their foot on the stool. Then lift the shoulder's head vigorously upwards, and pull the hand from the side of the patient; and have other assistants pinch at the shoulder's head so that it does not move backwards. That shoulder comes back now, and if you see that you are pulling it according to this manner: and let there be someone in attendance larger than the patient; and stand facing their side, and hold up their shoulder against the stool underneath them, then raise the stool upwards, so that the patient hangs at an angle; and have other assistants pull the hand from the side of the patient downwards towards their stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, so he cannot bear any weight with it, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And to reset it is also done in another manner: and you bury the long ember in the ground, so that the dislocated part stays as straight as a needle, but neither too large nor too curved; then place it under the patient, but with its tip touching a surface and the body not moving; and let the patient lie still for as long as the length of the rod; then stretch out their arm from the other side, forming, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it doesn't return due to all these things that we have said, this is your treatment: take an ember of two full lengths and three quarters of a width, which has a handle wide enough for both hands to enter and press against the socket, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie the stem near to the body where it's covered by cloth, so that the stem doesn't hurt the patient, then place the stem on the side opposite the dislocation; and extend your arm along the stem up to its end, and fasten the brace on the stem, and the arm at the head of the hand, then place the arm on one stick about as wide as a stick, and let the hand hang down below, and leave the torso hanging from the other side: the joint will now return in this manner.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, no matter how it was done, if it should be that you place upon the joint a rod of hair equal, then apply an adhesive plaster with ground powder from the mill, along with incense and egg yolk, over all the shoulder and around, then remove from the joint addition, and rebind over the plaster, and hold your hands in this way. And let your hands remain like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It should be that he eats little, until the limbs are strengthened, because it will heal faster; and then eat more after five days or seven, and move it; and if it is firm and it is not softened, it will be healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has moved out of its place because of moisture or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply three burnings to it, as was explained in our previous chapter about burnings.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't hold, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or extended or weakened; and know that the joint would never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocation near the buttocks, and breasts, or behind, is caused by pushing, extension of hands, and administration in another place; treatment should be applied as long as it's clean.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes redness to the limb, and delayed movements, then immerse the patient in hot baths many times, until that redness is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder joint issue
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and it returns to those points; if it has been dislocated from all sides, as well in front and behind, and dislocation does not respond because you can see it clearly and feel it clearly; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you connect the cut wound with healthy tissue, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and cannot bend the arm or reach his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you should reset it this way that the abscesses are closed, for if they were to be left open, there would be trouble in closing them; and sometimes it cannot be brought back completely, especially when it's at the back; it is worse than other dislocations and causes more pain, and by chance it brings death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And restoration occurs like this when you can bring it back: extend their hand with both of your hands; and their arms are spread out, and the hands face towards the body along the length of the forearm, in and out, and hold the joint at its natural place or at the base of the palm, until they return to their original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And when it comes to dislocation in front of the body, it returns as soon as he doubles his hand on his own and holds the joint at the base of the palm with a tool that is set back.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, apply strong extension; and when you administer this, extend the arm and hold it steady. If it does not move during the extension, then rotate the arm from each side, while having wrapped a double long and wide cloth around the joint; and when you aim to connect the joint with your hand, anoint it with oil to soften the joint. Then firmly set the joint in place until it recovers. Once it is back in place, cover it with dry plaster mixed with raw egg whites, hold it in position, allow its connection at the shoulder, and leave it for a few days, then remove the bandage.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, release the ligament and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not sit well, redo the plastering and the bandage, and let them stay like that for some more days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if they feel pain after putting the joint back in place, and it moves again, then bathe them well and rub vigorously, pressing until they are relieved. Or you put mutton fat on the joint for one day and one night, then apply oil, and have them take a bath; and when they sweat, gently rub the joint, then reapply the fat, and then enter into a bath; and do this process twice or three times, until they feel better; and if you can see that it has returned to its original state, then place wet cow's dung heated with butter on them. If this brings back its natural position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand dislocation has occurred and the recovery is faster than for other joints, throughout the body. It's necessary to return it to its place as soon as possible, while it's still dislocated, so that the fingers swell or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the process of putting it back in place involves placing your hand on the sick person's table and stretching out their other hand, positioning them evenly so that their palm is against the appearance of the joint. Hold it until all parts are renewed. You should then look to see if it's properly aligned; then place the sick person's back of their hand on a table for extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then have the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and you look to place his hand at the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that's good, if not, if the application of plaster poultices relieves abscesses and leaves him undisturbed, let him continue without restarting.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put him in the right position after some days, if the joint remains twisted; and it does not harm him as long as his hands are swollen, and he cannot exert any force: then know that a nerve has been cut, or an artery; there is no other reason except to apply heat cautery for this situation, and by chance there is no other option.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hands are in plaster, apply what we have said on plaster, then apply it and leave them for five days, then remove it and leave them as is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no pain, if the water is warm, and rub it until it becomes clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Regarding the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	None of the time is dislocated the shoulder blade on either side, none at the back of the palm or in the belly; thus is the shoulder blade and holds the dislocation until it revives. Then support the head of the shoulder blade and guide it towards the site where it was dislodged; and leave it two days, then put it equal that day; and fasten the joint if you have said, and then the dislocation of this day, and let it move and bind again. And do so repeatedly, until it is snugly fitted, and do likewise, if it is dislocated in the belly of the hand, do as you did before until it heals; and do so similarly, when it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Dislocation of the ankle, dislocation of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When it is dislocated in the back or neck, or when there are multiple dislocations, if no cure is applied, because time rushes the patient into harm.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the discharges jump without will, cannot be held back, and many times they soften one body part or both sides of each limb; or two out of four limbs; this which softens at three parts is called "gilbositez": The cure is that you reward if the gilbositez came in childhood: If there is no treatment or healing from the start.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And the one that has just given birth or been struck or by similar actions, according to old medical practices would speak in broad terms, not deriving any great benefit from it; but I have condensed it according to my intention and formed tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I state that in the birthing process where it comes out before the belly, nothing can be restored or healed; and likewise if it comes straight to the right side and cannot be cured except what is directly related to that which goes to the backside, as I say; and for the patient's condition should extend over their hips evenly in one direction and have tension beneath them so they do not get hurt; then stick a red hot needle into the head on soil formed and another at the heels, and tie strips between these and under the muscles near the soreness, and another around the hips and knees and ankles; two attendants should hold these strips, one at the head and the other at the heels, among the two needles; and they must be well fastened, the needle as we said earlier, and you place your palms on the backside until she regains consciousness.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it doesn't return through this treatment, take a three-foot long board and place it over the surface, and have the patient lying on their side, with the sick person facing towards the edge. Place the head of the board over the spine, then put the middle of the board over the backbone; and set the eyes at each end of the board, and press well until they return to position; and if you see fit, perform the twist around the wrist that turns into the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And if you insert two thorns into the middle of the sick person's arm, at each hand and place space between each thorn, about one long's palm; in each thorn is a loop or bend where the wrist turns, making sure the thorns are firmly buried so they don't move; between these two thorns you place one turning thorn, with which it aligns when turned, and place two smaller thorns of one long's palm between the turning thorns to turn the wrist; then tie a band between the loops at the wrist towards the arm, and another band from the loops at the hands to the other wrist, and each servant turns their wrist all along the band; and the masters shall make the spine equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are equal, if you put dried plaster on them with plenty of egg, and then the powdery substance, and then the ash from a tablet made up of three inches in length, that treats the pusiness area and the healthy part of the vertebrae, then tie it with a string, as we have said, and the patient uses subtle bleeding therapy until they are sound. And if anything comes towards the end of soundness, it should administer softening and soothing medicines along with the therapy we mentioned before; and whenever you administer one piece of plaster, and there is no appearance in the lower vertebrae of the back, take care that this is dislocation; because it's the bone that opens up, so you shouldn't have any presumption: by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder only suffer dislocations, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: internally and externally, in front and behind; and more internally elsewhere, and less dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation from within is that when you unite the diseased leg with the healthy one, it extends further, and opens more for the diseased knee than the healthy one, and cannot make the diseased knee bend to the back; and it is the limbs that are swollen under the abscesses because the kneecap of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who approaches death, so it is that this event is contrary to what was before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who is coming towards death are such that his leg is well according to its fulfillment; still though, he does not double bend his knee without pain, and if you try to make him walk, he cannot move forward and retains his urine, and swells at his ankle, and when he walks, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who is behind are such that he cannot spread his knee or double it, and that leg is more curved than the other, and his ankle is flattened, and that shoulder comes up under his back.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The correction of this semblance of dislocation involves you rewarding it if the dislocation is old and remains according to its position, without any treatment needed; and there should be no assumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those whose dislocation is recent, and there are four ways of dislocation, if you act quickly to restore the joint, and stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it towards the right and left; perhaps if it returns on its own and no further treatment is needed.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must apply the strong minister and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie one hand above the knee; and another minister extends their hand over them like they are rubbing their thighs together, then pushes their hands upwards against their knees; and another holds onto the cord at the other end; and extend everything up and down all at once until the diseased leg lifts off the ground completely and stays suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is typical for four similar situations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it's correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then care must be taken based on its appearance When the shoulder is dislocated from the collarbone, you need to place the patient's healthy side against their back, then attach the bandage at the base of the elbow, and above the armpit, then continue wrapping it upwards towards the armpit, moving downwards too. Then hold another assistant's hands, grasp firmly on the fatty part of the elbow, and stretch out in a forward position: if they return to their normal position now; this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you can't secure it in this way as we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together tightly with a strong rope around both heels and knees, making sure that the diseased leg is extended more than twice the length of the other; then hang him up by his head using a pole, and extend outwards both his arms to their full length; then command one assistant to hold onto the elbow part of the limb, while others assist with the patient hanging, holding firmly on the limb itself as if in embrace. For the joint is now coming back quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are at the back, if the patient lies down, as we have said in those with glibosity, and tightens the bandage on the diseased leg properly, and also around the ankle; then place two hot sticks, one at the head and another at the heels. Then stick a pin between the buttocks of the diseased side in its shape; and has moist cloths under it to prevent it from chafing the patient's skin, then extend each part towards him, and place the dislocation as evenly as possible with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it doesn't, place on .ie., the table, and press on it like we said in glibosity, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be extended as quickly as possible, following what I have said; and place their suffering limb on the back of their shoulder blade, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards their knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is behind, it does not fit to extend the limb below or lift it from the ground, instead it should remain in a position as if the hip had been dislocated backwards, just like we have said about lying on both hips; and stay there on its back, and let the bandage be extended as we stated previously, and press onto the joint at the table; and will be right when the limb extends its legs, and they are equal; then adjust the knees, put in the plaster, tie it tightly with a band, so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then release it, and place the plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, retighten it as before, and let it be rested for three more days; then release it, and make him walk well until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint can be dislocated in three ways: one should know that it can dislocate internally and externally, and behind; and does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs for this are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee. If they do not lock at their knee, know that it is dislocated; and for restoration of all such actions, have the patient sit straight up, extend their leg if possible, place your back against their thigh, and set their foot on your feet. Then take their knee between your hands, pull it apart with your fingers, then bend both sides tightly at the knee; and another assistant extends their foot until the knees return to their place, and the signs are that they properly bend their leg lightly at their knee; apply a plaster, make the leg rest against the thigh, and keep them together tightly for three or four days, then release; and do not move the patient's limbs again until the muscles have been strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, apply strong extension, as we have said about treating the hip, until it becomes stable.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never perfectly reduced or completely dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tries to move towards the part where it has dislocated: the realignment should be quick, and one must gently extend it with their hands only when it seems stable.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is successfully realigned, have the patient sit straight, and guide the person by their ankles upwards from the ankle; then pull the leg towards you with your right hand, and then twice with your left. Then extend them upwards high, firmly buckle the leg up there; do this twice as we said previously, pulling and moving the leg while buckling it. If it returns, that's good; if not, start again because it will return; and if it can't return like this, have the person lie down on their back with the ankle under them, firmly plant one foot in the ground between their legs, and tie cloths around to prevent any bruising of the ankle. Then guide your assistants' hands near the ankle joint, and others guide the healthy leg downwards at its knee bend until they are tied onto the leg; then extend each assistant's hands equally while keeping the ankle under you for holding the ankle when extending it; finally place the dislocated ankle joints equally in their hands, and have another assistant cut around the healthy knee joint and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at the point, place the bandage and seal it upwards, hold tightly in form, fasten the heel to the leg, and guard against nerves located behind the ankle that they are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if they loosen, remove them. Then release on the third day or fourth, and warn the patient off for another four days; and if he progresses beyond this stage, it is not certain that he has not dislocated again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses are pressing on him and it comes to this, you must soothe him, as we have said elsewhere, until he feels better.
des dois	Of the fire cautery, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, if they need to be properly stretched as part of their work, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in neither the neck nor the foot, you should have the patient sit upright or on a flat surface completely straight, and place his foot where it opens from these joints, then press with your foot until he revives. And when he has recovered equally and nothing appears, place under the sole of the foot a board for shoulders, then press firmly, and let him rest for three days, then release him; and make him rest until he is in good health.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding wound care and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When there is a wound that comes with dislocation and you wish to restore it, many times it was seen that the patient died: if you are not presumptuous in the treatment, if you do not possess knowledge in this art and have not used it for long periods of time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and delayed, but rather rash; then at the beginning use calms to relieve the wound heat, and let the patient be with God's hand if you don't see hope for recovery; and when you do see hope, now reset the limb back into place in such a way that allows the healing heat of the wound to circulate; and once the limb is back in place, then use calms to relieve the wound heat again, treat the wound properly as required with dried ointments; and if there was breakage due to dislocation, and small bones were broken, fix them and do what we have said for simple diseases; and guard yourself against entering a path of fear, according to what I've spoken about earlier, because this leads you towards actions according to your Creator, and with the wisdom you arm yourself and your body.
Amen	Amen
